Proof That Permanence Is an Additional Meaning
Provides logical proof that permanence is an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that permanence is an additional attribute distinct from the essence, and why this distinction matters for arguments about the temporality of the world.

Core Idea
Permanence is not existence; it is an additional attribute separable from the essence.

This passage presents the core rational proof that permanence (بقاء) is an additional meaning beyond the essence, not identical to existence. The author begins by noting consensus that a substance at its first moment is not described as permanent, then draws an analogy with motion to show that permanence is an acquired attribute. Finally, he warns that denying this distinction would undermine the entire proof for the temporality of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its flow. Then read the translation. Note the initial claim and the consensus cited.
The passage is dense with citations from Mu'tazila scholars.
2
Identify the key definitions
Find the definitions of permanence given by Abu Ali al-Jubba'i, followers of Abu Hashim, and al-Khayyat. Note how they all agree that permanence is attributed after existence.
These definitions show that even opponents consider permanence separate from initial existence.
3
Understand the analogy with motion
The author uses motion as an analogy: just as a substance is initially not moving and then moves, proving motion is additional, so too a substance is initially not permanent and then becomes permanent.
This analogy is central to the proof.
4
Grasp the consequences of denial
The author warns that if permanence were not additional, then the substance would never be without it, which would invalidate evidence for accidents and thus the proof for the world's temporality.
This shows the high stakes of this theological distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على أن البقاء معنى زائد على ذات الباقي أن الجوهر في أول أحوال وجوده غير مستحق للوصف بالبقاء انعقد عليه الإجماع بيننا وبين الجمهور من حذاقهم حتى قال أبو علي الجبائي: البقاء هو الوجود عن وجوده. وقال أصحاب أبي هاشم الباقي هو الموجود الذي قد أتى عليه زمان، وحكى مثل هذا القول عن أبي الحسين الخياط رئيس البغدادية من المعتزلة، وقال بعض أصحاب أبي هاشم الباقي هو الموجود الذي لم يحدث في حال الإخبار بالوجود، ثم يوصف بعد ذلك بالبقاء، ولو لم يكن البقاء معنى زائدًا على الذات لما انفك الوصف بالبقاء عن وجود الذات كما في الوجود، وعكسه الحركة فإن الجوهر في أول أحوال وجوده لما كان غير موصوف بالحركة ثم اتصف بعد ذلك بها علم أنها معنى زائد على الذات فكذا البقاء، ولو بطل أن يكون البقاء معنى زائدًا على مع وجود الذات تارة متعريًا عن الوصف به بل مستحيل الوصف به لبطلت الدلالة على ثبوت الأعراض بطلان الدلالة على حدوث العالم إذ بثبوتها وتحقق حدوثها يستدل على حدوث الجواهر. والذي يحقق هذا أن عبارة القدرية في إثبات التفرقة بين صفة النفس وبين صفة المعنى أن صفة النفس ما لزمه ووصف المعنى ما جاز خروجه
And the proof that permanence is an additional meaning beyond the essence of the permanent is that the substance in the first state of its existence is not deserving of the description of permanence; there is consensus on this between us and the majority of their experts. So much so that Abu Ali al-Jubba'i said: "Permanence is existence from its existence." And the followers of Abu Hashim said: "The permanent is that which has had time pass over it." And a similar statement is reported from Abu al-Husayn al-Khayyat, the chief of the Baghdadiyya among the Mu'tazila. And some followers of Abu Hashim said: "The permanent is that which has not come into existence at the time of reporting its existence, then it is described after that with permanence." And if permanence were not an additional meaning beyond the essence, then the description of permanence would not be separate from the existence of the essence, as in the case of existence. And the opposite is motion, for when the substance in the first state of its existence is not described with motion, then is described with it afterwards, it is known that it is an additional meaning beyond the essence; likewise permanence. And if it were invalid that permanence be an additional meaning beyond the essence, such that at times the essence is bare of the description of it, rather impossible to be so described, then the evidence for the existence of accidents would be invalid, and the evidence for the temporality of the world would be invalid, for by their existence and the verification of their temporality one deduces the temporality of substances. And what verifies this is the statement of the Qadariyya in establishing the distinction between the attribute of the self and the attribute of meaning: that the attribute of the self is what is inseparable, and the attribute of meaning is what can cease.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage provides the main proof that permanence (بقاء) is an additional meaning (معنى زائد) beyond the essence, not identical to it. The argument begins with a consensus: a substance (جوهر) at the first moment of its existence is not described as permanent. The author cites leading Mu'tazila figures (Abu Ali al-Jubba'i, Abu Hashim's followers, al-Khayyat) who, despite their different definitions, agree that permanence is only attributed after existence. If permanence were not additional, it would be inseparable like existence itself. The analogy with motion (حركة) is used: just as a substance is initially not moving and then moves, showing motion is additional, so too permanence is additional because a substance is initially not permanent and then becomes so. If permanence were not additional, then the substance would never be described without it, which is false. The author then warns that denying the additional nature of permanence would undermine the proof for the existence of accidents and thus the proof for the temporality (حدوث) of the world, since accidents' temporality indicates substances' temporality. Finally, he notes that the Qadariyya (here meaning Mu'tazila) themselves distinguish between attribute of the self (صفة النفس) which is inseparable, and attribute of meaning (صفة المعنى) which can cease. Permanence, being separable from the essence, falls under attribute of meaning.

Misconception: Permanence is identical to existence.
Correction: Permanence is an additional attribute because a substance can exist without being described as permanent at the first moment, as shown by consensus and analogy with motion.

Checkpoint
What is the key analogy used to prove that permanence is an additional meaning?
A) Existence and non-existence.
B) Motion and rest.
C) Motion and permanence.
D) Color and flavor.

Key Takeaway
Permanence is an additional attribute to the essence, not identical to existence, and this distinction is foundational for proofs of the temporality of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You exist right now, but the lesson shows that permanence is not automatically yours. Are you living as if your existence is guaranteed to continue? How does the truth that only God has essential permanence change your attitude toward each breath you take?
?
The proof uses the fact that a substance initially lacks permanence. Think of a moment in your life when you felt 'permanent'—a job, a relationship, your health. Given this lesson, how might you re-evaluate that feeling? What concrete step can you take today to rely less on your own permanence and more on the Eternal?
?
The Mu'tazila distinguished attributes that can cease from those that cannot. Reflect on your own attributes: your knowledge, your patience, your faith. Which of these do you mistakenly treat as unchanging? How can you actively work on maintaining them rather than assuming they will persist?

The Proof that Remaining is an Additional Attribute
Al-Nasafi argues that remaining (baqa') is an additional attribute (ma'na) over the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that remaining (baqa') is an additional attribute over the essence, not identical to existence.

Core Idea
Remaining is not just existence; it is an extra attribute that time makes necessary.

Al-Nasafi presents a careful argument that remaining cannot be reduced to existence itself. He points to a universal agreement that a substance at the first moment of its existence is not described as 'remaining'. This shows that remaining requires a separate attribute added to existence over time. Let's trace his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the background
Al-Nasafi begins by distinguishing attributes that are inseparable from the essence (like existence) from those that are additional. This sets up the need to prove that remaining is among the latter.
The opening phrase 'returning to the essence' indicates attributes that cannot be separated.
2
Identify the consensus
The author notes that all theologians agree that a substance in its first moment does not deserve the description 'remaining'. This is a key premise.
He cites Mu'tazilite definitions that equate remaining with existence over time.
3
Analyze the analogy with movement
He compares remaining to movement: just as movement is an additional attribute because a body can exist without it, so remaining must be additional because a substance exists initially without being described as remaining.
This analogical argument strengthens the case.
4
See the theological implication
Al-Nasafi warns that if this reasoning were rejected, the entire proof of the world's temporal origin (via accidents) would collapse.
This shows the high stakes of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راجعا إلى الذات كالوجود والشيئية واللونية والعرضية، ولا توصف بما كان معنى زائدًا على الذات والدليل على أن البقاء معنى زائد على ذات الباقي أن الجوهر في أول أحوال وجوده غير مستحق للوصف بالبقاء انعقد عليه الإجماع بيننا وبين الجمهور من حذاقهم حتى قال أبو علي الجبائي: البقاء هو الوجود عن وجوده. وقال أصحاب أبي هاشم الباقي هو الموجود الذي قد أتى عليه زمان، وحكى مثل هذا القول عن أبي الحسين الخياط رئيس البغدادية من المعتزلة، وقال بعض أصحاب أبي هاشم الباقي هو الموجود الذي لم يحدث في حال الإخبار بالوجود، ثم يوصف بعد ذلك بالبقاء، ولو لم يكن البقاء معنى زائدًا على الذات لما انفك الوصف بالبقاء عن وجود الذات كما في الوجود، وعكسه الحركة فإن الجوهر في أول أحوال وجوده لما كان غير موصوف بالحركة ثم اتصف بعد ذلك بها علم أنها معنى زائد على الذات فكذا البقاء، ولو بطل أن يكون البقاء معنى زائدًا على مع وجود الذات تارة متعريًا عن الوصف به بل مستحيل الوصف به لبطلت الدلالة على ثبوت الأعراض بطلان الدلالة على حدوث العالم إذ بثبوتها وتحقق حدوثها يستدل على حدوث الجواهر.
Returning to the essence, like existence, thingness, colorness, and accidentalness, and it is not described with what is a meaning additional to the essence. And the proof that remaining is a meaning additional to the essence of the Remaining One is that the substance in the first state of its existence is not deserving of the description of remaining; there is consensus upon this between us and the majority of their experts, such that Abu Ali al-Jubbai said: 'Remaining is existence from its existence.' And the followers of Abu Hashim said: 'The remaining one is the existent which time has passed over.' And a similar saying was related from Abu al-Husayn al-Khayyat, the head of the Baghdad school of the Mu'tazila. And some followers of Abu Hashim said: 'The remaining one is the existent which did not come to be at the moment of reporting its existence, then it is described after that with remaining.' And if remaining were not a meaning additional to the essence, the description of remaining would never be separate from the existence of the essence, as in the case of existence. The opposite is movement, for the substance in the first state of its existence, since it was not described with movement, then became described with it after that, it is known that it is a meaning additional to the essence; so too with remaining. And if it were invalid that remaining is a meaning additional to the existence of the essence sometimes being devoid of the description of it, rather impossible to be described with it, then the indication of the establishment of accidents would be invalidated, the invalidation of the indication of the origination of the world, since by their establishment and the verification of their origination one infers the origination of substances.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a proof that remaining (baqa') is an additional attribute (ma'na) added to the essence (dhat), not the essence itself. The author begins by noting that some attributes like existence and thingness are essentially inseparable from the essence and cannot be separated; they are not described as additional meanings. Then he states the proof that remaining is an additional meaning: the substance (jawhar) at the first moment of its existence is not deserving of the description 'remaining'. This is universally agreed upon, including by Mu'tazilite figures like Abu Ali al-Jubbai and Abu Hashim, who all define 'remaining' in terms of existence over time. If remaining were identical to the essence, then a substance would always be described as remaining as long as it exists, just as it is always described as existent. But it is not; at the first instant, it exists but cannot be called 'remaining'. This is analogous to movement: a substance begins existence without movement, then later movement occurs, proving movement is an extra attribute. Similarly, for a substance to change from not-being-described-with-remaining to being-described-with-remaining, there must be an additional attribute. Finally, the author argues that if it were impossible for a substance to be described with remaining at its first moment, then the argument from the existence of accidents to prove the temporal origin of the world would collapse, because accidents (which are essential to proving that substances are created) rely on this logic.

Misconception: Some think that 'remaining' is simply continued existence and not a separate attribute.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that if remaining were just existence, it would accompany existence from the first moment, but it does not, proving it is an additional attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that it is impossible for a substance to be described with remaining at the very first moment of its existence?
A) Because remaining requires time to have passed.
B) Because the substance does not exist at that moment.
C) Because remaining is identical to existence.
D) Because the attribute of remaining only applies to God.

Key Takeaway
Remaining is an additional attribute because a substance at its first moment exists without being described as remaining, proving it is not identical to existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You exist right now, but does your existence guarantee that you will remain? Every moment you are dependent on Allah's continuous act of creation. If remaining were just existence, you would be self-sustaining. How does this truth force you to rely on Allah every second? Commit to making du'a for steadfastness (thabat) today.
?
The substance at the first moment exists but cannot be called 'remaining'. Reflect on your own life: at birth you existed but could you claim to 'remain'? Your life is a series of moments given by Allah. How will you use today's fleeting existence to prepare for an eternal meeting with Him? Decide on one action that will have lasting value.
?
If you deny that remaining is an additional attribute, the entire proof for the world's creation collapses. What is at stake for you personally? Do you truly believe that Allah's attributes are real and distinct, or do you treat them as mere concepts? This lesson demands that you take Allah's perfection seriously. What will you do today to increase your reverence for His names and attributes?

Responding to the Objection: Change Necessarily Requires an Additional Attribute
Al-Nasafi refutes the objection that change does not always imply an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's refutation of the claim that change in a substance does not always necessitate an additional attribute.

Core Idea
If a description is impossible with the essence, it must come from an external meaning.

The objector tries to argue that when change is inevitable from the first moment, no extra attribute is needed. Al-Nasafi responds by showing that the impossibility of description at any point reveals dependence on a meaning, not the essence. This lesson unpacks his logical rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector claims that change requires an additional attribute only if the substance could exist without that description at some time. If change is necessary from the start, no extra attribute is needed.
This objection challenges the need for an external cause of change.
2
Grasp Al-Nasafi's key distinction
Al-Nasafi explains that being described (ittisaf) is either due to the essence itself or due to a meaning. If the essence exists but the description is impossible, it cannot be from the essence; it must be from a meaning.
The impossibility of description is the crucial evidence.
3
See the analogy with blackness
Al-Nasafi uses the example of blackness existing in a substance but the substance cannot be described as black, then later becomes black. This absurdity proves that change always requires an external meaning.
This confirms the objector's scenario is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسأل بعضهم: إن تغير الجوهر عما كان عليه إنما يوجب التغير بوجود معنى زائد على الذات إذا جاز وجود الجوهر متعريًا عن ذلك الوصف أوقاتًا، فأما إذا لم يجز تعريه عنه ولا وقتا واحدًا ووجب تغيره في الثاني من حال حدوثه لا محالة لم يجب به حدوث معنى فيه. قلنا هذا كلام من لا يدري ما يقول، وهذا لأن الاتصاف إما أن يكون لأجل الذات، وإما أن يكون لمعنى، وإذا وجد الذات واستحال الاتصاف علم أن الاتصاف ليس من موجبات الذات، فعلم أنه من موجبات المعنى لأن الذات لو وجد وانعدم جواز الاتصاف كان الاتصاف من موجبات المعنى دون الذات، فإذا مع كان الاتصاف مستحيلاً مع وجود الذات كان أولى أن يكون الاتصاف موجب معنى وراء الذات لا موجب الذات. يحققه أن الاتصاف لو كان من موجبات الذات وقد وجدت الذات واستحال الاتصاف لكان فيه القول باستحالة ثبوت الحكم، وإن تحققت العلة وهذا ظاهر الفساد ولو جاز هذا لجاز أن يقوم السواد بذات ويستحيل اتصافه بأنه أسود ثم في الزمان الثاني يجب اتصافه به وهذا محال لم يقل به أحد من العقلاء.
And some of them asked: 'The change of the substance from what it was only necessitates change due to the existence of a meaning additional to the essence if it is possible for the substance to exist stripped of that description at times. As for if it is not possible for it to be stripped of it at any single time, and its change in the second moment of its origination is necessary without fail, then the occurrence of a meaning in it is not necessitated.' We said: This is the speech of one who does not know what he says. And this is because the description [being described] is either on account of the essence, or on account of a meaning. And when the essence exists and it is impossible to be described, it is known that the description is not from the necessaries of the essence, so it is known that it is from the necessaries of the meaning. Because if the essence existed and the possibility of description were absent, the description would be from the necessaries of the meaning, not from the essence. So when the description is impossible with the existence of the essence, it is more fitting that the description is a necessitation of a meaning beyond the essence, not a necessitation of the essence. That which verifies this is that if the description were from the necessaries of the essence, and the essence existed and the description were impossible, then this would entail saying the impossibility of the establishment of the judgment while the cause is realized, and this is clearly corrupt. And if this were permissible, then it would be permissible that blackness subsists in a substance and it is impossible for it to be described as black, then in a second moment its description with it becomes necessary, and this is impossible; no rational person has said it.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding whether change in a substance necessarily implies an additional attribute. The objector argues that change requires an additional attribute only if the substance could have existed without that description at some time. But if it is impossible for the substance to ever be stripped of that description, and change occurs necessarily in the second moment of its origination, then no additional attribute is required. The author rejects this as ignorance. He explains that being described (al-ittisaf) is either due to the essence itself or due to a meaning. If the essence exists but the description is impossible, then the description cannot be a necessary consequence of the essence; it must come from a meaning. Even if the possibility of description is absent (i.e., the description is not possible at that moment), if the essence exists and the description is impossible, that still indicates the description depends on a meaning. To clarify, the author gives an analogy: if blackness exists in a substance but it is impossible for that substance to be described as black, and then later it becomes necessarily described as black, this would be absurd. Therefore, the objector's scenario is impossible, and change always requires an additional attribute when there is a shift from impossibility to possibility of description.

Key Terms
تغير
جوهر
ذات
معنى
اتصاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Change in a substance can occur without an additional attribute if the change is necessary from the first moment.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that even if change is necessary from the start, the impossibility of the description at any point proves it depends on an external meaning, not the essence.

Checkpoint
What is the example the author uses to illustrate the absurdity of the objector's position?
A) A substance that is white but cannot be described as white.
B) Blackness subsisting in a substance that cannot be described as black.
C) A substance that is always in motion.
D) The existence of God without attributes.

Key Takeaway
Change always requires an external meaning because if a description is impossible despite the existence of the essence, the description must come from something beyond the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a quality you believe you lack but desperately need—like true humility or gratitude. You exist, so if this quality were from your essence, it would be present. But it is not. Where does it come from? What external meaning must you seek to acquire it, and how will you actively pursue it today?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that when a description is impossible despite the existence of the essence, the description must come from something beyond the essence. What if the description in question is your own 'faith'? Do you assume your faith is a necessary part of your essence, or do you acknowledge it depends on an external cause—and if so, how will you secure that cause?
?
If you claim to believe something but find that belief impossible to act upon, what does that reveal about the source of that belief? Are you willing to accept that the change you need cannot come from within, and that you must turn to an external meaning—the very Source of all meaning—to transform you?

The Absurdity of Attributes Arising Without Change
Al-Nasafi presents a conditional argument leading to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Nasafi argues that if an essence does not necessitate an attribute in the first state, it cannot necessitate it in the second state without a change, and how this leads to absurd consequences.

Core Idea
The same essence cannot spontaneously produce an attribute it didn't have before.

Al-Nasafi opens his argument with a logical dilemma about the relationship between an essence and its attributes. He shows that if an essence does not necessitate a certain attribute at the first moment of its existence, it cannot later spontaneously acquire that attribute without some change or new cause. This reasoning forms a cornerstone of the Maturidi position on attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening hypothetical
Read the first sentence where Al-Nasafi sets up the conditional situation: essence does not necessitate attribute in first state, then same essence in second state cannot cause attribute without change.
2
Follow the absurd consequence
Notice how he extrapolates: if it did cause attribute without change, then inability would lead to power, ignorance to knowledge.
3
Reflect on the absurdity
Ask yourself why this is impossible. The conclusion is that change in attributes must come from an external cause or inherent change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الذات لو لم توجب وجود الاتصاف في الأول ثم في الثاني عين ذلك الذات الذي لم يوجب الاتصاف واستحال وجود الاتصاف معه أوجب الاتصاف من غير تغيير ولا حدوث معنى فيه لوجب أن يقال : إن العجز وإن وجد في أول أحوال وجوده و استحال اتصاف الذات الذي قام به العجز بكونه قادرًا يوجب في الثاني كونه قادرا ، وكذا الذات الذي قام به الجهل يوجب كون الذات في الثاني عالمًا وإن استحال اتصافه في أول الأحوال، وهذا محال.

ثم يقال لهم : الوصف الذي كان يجوز كون الجوهر متعريًا عند أوقاتا لم كان وصف المعنى؟ ألأجل أنه إذا انعدم مع وجود الذات علم أنه ليس من موجبات الذات أم لأجل معنى آخر؟

فإن قال بالثاني، كلف إبرازه ولا قدره له عليه، وإن قال بالأول فقد أقر بما يوجب بطلان سؤاله هذا، وظهر أن لا فرق بين جواز التعري وقتا واحدًا وبين جوازه أوقاتا كثيرة.

ثم يقال : لو كان بغير الوصف مع جواز بقائه متعريا عنه يوجب حدوث معنى كان بغيره مع استحالة بقائه متعريًا عنه أولى، ولولا حدوث المعنى الذي اضطر إلى تغير وصفه لجاز وجوده على ما كان عليه قبله.

ثم يقال لهم : إذا استحال كون الجوهر متحركاً أو ساكنا في حال الحدوث و استحال بقاؤه عليه متعريًا عنهما بعد لم يحتج إلى حدوث معنى من أجله صار متحركًا أو ساكنا، فإذا كان هذا مستحيلاً ولم يكن جائزا عند أهل التوحيد ولم يكن بد من القول بوجود الحركة أو السكون دل ذلك على بعض ما قلتموه.
He establishes that if the essence did not necessitate the existence of being qualified in the first [state], and then in the second [state] it is the same essence that did not necessitate being qualified, and the existence of being qualified with it is impossible, but [if] it necessitates being qualified without any change or occurrence of a meaning in it, then it would be necessary to say: Indeed inability, even if it exists in the first state of its existence, and it is impossible for the essence in which inability subsists to be described as powerful, necessitates in the second [state] that it is powerful. Similarly, the essence in which ignorance subsists necessitates that the essence becomes knowing in the second [state] even though its being qualified is impossible in the first state. And this is impossible.

Then it is said to them: The description that it was permissible for the substance to be bare of at times? Why was it described by the attribute? Because if it [the attribute] does not exist with the existence of the essence, it is known that it is not among the necessaries of the essence? Or for another meaning?

If they say the second, they are required to produce it, and they have no power to do so. If they say the first, they have admitted what necessitates the invalidity of their question, and it becomes clear that there is no difference between the permissibility of being bare at one time and its permissibility at many times.

Then it is said: If it were by the description [only] with the permissibility of its remaining bare of it, it would necessitate the occurrence of a meaning; but by other than the description, with the impossibility of its remaining bare of it, it is more fitting. And were it not for the occurrence of the meaning that compelled the change of its description, its existence would be permissible as it was before.

Then it is said to them: If it is impossible for the substance to be moving or stationary in the state of origination, and it is impossible for it to remain upon it bare of them afterward, then it does not need the occurrence of a meaning for which it becomes moving or stationary. So if this is impossible and is not permissible according to the people of tawhid, and there is no alternative but to affirm the existence of motion or rest, that indicates some of what you have said.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step argument establishing that a substance (jawhar) cannot be devoid of attributes at the first moment of its existence. The author begins with a hypothetical: if the essence (dhat) does not necessitate being qualified (ittisaf) in the first state, and the same essence is present in the second state, then it cannot necessitate being qualified in the second state without a change. If it did, then inability would have to produce power, and ignorance would have to produce knowledge, which is absurd. The author then poses a dilemma to the opponent: why can a substance be bare of a description at some times? Is it because the absence of the attribute shows it is not necessitated by the essence, or for some other reason? If the opponent says the latter, they must produce that reason, which they cannot. If they say the former, they admit that being bare at one time is no different from being bare at many times, which undermines their objection. Next, the author argues that if a substance could remain bare of an attribute without an intervening attribute, then the occurrence of a new attribute would be more necessary when it cannot remain bare. Without that attribute, the substance would remain unchanged. Finally, the author gives the example of motion and rest: a substance cannot be moving or stationary at the moment of origination (huduth), and it cannot remain bare of both afterward. Therefore, an attribute (motion or rest) must occur. This proves the necessity of attributes for substances at every moment.

Key Terms
الذات
الاتصاف
العجز
الجهل
القدرة
العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reasoning in this passage, if an essence does not necessitate an attribute in the first state, what would happen if it later required that attribute without any change?
A) It would prove the essence is eternal.
B) Inability would produce power and ignorance would produce knowledge.
C) The attribute would be eternal.
D) The essence would cease to exist.

Key Takeaway
An essence cannot acquire a new attribute without a change or external cause; otherwise, opposite attributes would arise from each other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat Allah's attributes as if they could change—for example, hoping His mercy will override His justice without any reason? How does this lesson's logic challenge that assumption?
?
Consider a sin you struggle with: do you expect to overcome it without any internal or external change, simply because 'you are still you'? What change must happen for you to acquire the attribute of piety?
?
If an essence cannot acquire a new attribute without a cause, what does that imply about your own spiritual transformation? Are you relying on a real cause (e.g., sincere repentance, divine aid) or just hoping for spontaneous change?

The Dilemma of Being Bare of Attributes
Al-Nasafi presents a dilemma to the opponent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses a dilemma to show that if a substance can be bare of an attribute at one time, it can be bare at many times, undermining the opponent's objection.

Core Idea
If bareness is possible once, it's possible always.

In this part of the argument, Al-Nasafi engages in a dialectical exchange with opponents who claim that a substance can be temporarily bare of attributes. He presents them with a dilemma: either the reason for the permissibility of bareness is that the attribute is not necessitated by the essence, or there is some other reason. Whichever they choose, they fall into contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's position
The opponent suggests that a substance can be bare of a description at some times. Note this.
2
Analyze the dilemma
Al-Nasafi poses two options: either the absence of the attribute shows it's not from the essence's necessaries, or there is another cause.
3
See the implications
If they choose the first, they admit no difference between being bare at one time or many. If the second, they cannot produce that other cause. Either way, their objection fails.

Source Text

?

?
When you think about Allah's attributes, do you ever subconsciously treat some as if they could be absent or optional? How does the logical structure of this dilemma challenge you to reconsider whether any of Allah's attributes are non-essential?
?
This lesson argues that if bareness is possible once, it is possible always. Is there a belief or value you hold that you have only ever applied inconsistently? What would it cost you to be consistent?

The Necessity of Attributes: The Example of Motion and Rest
Al-Nasafi uses motion and rest as a concrete example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the example of motion and rest to demonstrate that a substance cannot be devoid of all attributes at any moment.

Core Idea
A substance cannot be neither moving nor stationary, forcing it to have one attribute.

In the final part of his argument, Al-Nasafi provides a concrete example from physics: a substance (atom) at the moment of its origination cannot be described as either moving or stationary. Yet, it cannot remain without either attribute afterward. Therefore, an attribute of motion or rest must occur, proving the necessity of attributes for substances.

Guided Path
1
Understand the example
Al-Nasafi points out that at the moment of origination, a substance cannot be moving or stationary.
2
Consider the impossibility of bareness
After origination, it cannot remain bare of both motion and rest.
3
Conclude the necessity
Therefore, an attribute (motion or rest) must occur, confirming that substances always have attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage forces you to admit that a substance cannot remain neutral—it must either be in motion or at rest. If your soul is the substance of your actions, what is its state right now? Is it moving towards obedience or resting in contentment with your Lord—or are you pretending there is a third option?
?
When you consider your own existence, you cannot be 'bare' of purpose or intention. Every moment you are either moving closer to Allah or drifting away. Which movement are you choosing right now, and what meaning (ma'na) did you just acquire?
?
The argument here is about a metaphysical truth, but it points to a spiritual reality: you were not created to remain attribute-less. You are always acquiring—either good or bad. If you were to die in this very moment, what would the description of your soul be—moving towards Allah or stationary in heedlessness? Commit to one attribute today.

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
Refuting baqa' as an inherent attribute from the first moment
Al-Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya and al-Saymari on baqa' being inherent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that baqa' (endurance) cannot be an inherent attribute from the first moment, using linguistic and rational arguments.

Core Idea
Endurance is not existence; language itself shows they are distinct.

In this passage, al-Nasafi responds to an objection from the Karramiyya and al-Saymari, who claim that a substance is described with endurance from the very first moment of existence, just as it is described with existence. He refutes them by appealing to linguistic usage and consensus, demonstrating that endurance is an additional attribute that can be absent while existence remains.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the objection is presented, then al-Nasafi distinguishes between two groups of opponents.
Pay attention to how the author sets up the refutation.
2
Identify the first linguistic argument
Find the argument about the phrase 'it existed and did not endure'. Understand why it would be contradictory if endurance were identical to existence.
This uses the principle of non-contradiction.
3
Identify the second linguistic argument
Look at the supplication example ('abqaka Allah' vs 'awjadaka Allah') and the synonymy of 'al-baqi' and 'al-da'im'. See how linguistic practice shows they are different.
Consensus of linguists is invoked here.
4
Grasp the accusation against opponents
Notice that al-Nasafi accuses the opponents of denying self-evident truths and breaking consensus. Reflect on why he considers their position so problematic.
This shows the seriousness of the doctrinal error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : هذا الاستدلال مبني على مقدمة مجحودة وهي: أنكم ادعيتم استحالة الوصف بالبقاء في حالة الوجود ، وهذا غير مسلم عند الكرامية فإنهم يزعمون أن الجوهر في أول أحوال وجوده موصوفا بالبقاء كما هو موصوف بالوجود، وإلى هذا القول يذهب عباد الصيمري صاحب هشام بن عمرو من جملة المعتزلة، كذا حكى عنه الكعبي في المقالات.

قلنا: إن المخالفين لنا في المسألة من رؤساء المعتزلة سلموا لنا هذا الذي بنينا فتكلمنا على ما مر معهم بناء على تسليمهم.

فأما الكرامية والصيمري فإنا نقول لهم: هذا منكم جحد الضروريات وإنكار البداهة، وخرق إجماع أهل اللسان قاطبة، فإنهم يستجيزون أن يقولوا وجد كذا ولم يبق ولو كان البقاء راجعًا إلى الذات كالوجود لكان قول القائل وجد ولم يبق كقول القائل وجد ولم يوجد وحيث عد هذا تناقضا دون الأول، دل على بطلان هذا الرأي المستنزل المحدث.

وكذا الناس يقولون في الدعاء : أبقاك الله، ولا يستجيز أحد أن يقول لآخر : أوجدك الله، ولو كان اللفظان في الحقيقة راجعين إلى شيء واحد لما امتنعوا عن إطلاق أحدهما الأطباق على إجازة إطلاق الآخر، وكذا الباقي والدائم من جملة الألفاظ المترادفة، ثم انعقد الإجماع على استحالة إطلاق لفظ الدائم فكذا الباقي.
For it is said: This inference is based on a premise that is disputed, namely that you claim the impossibility of being described with endurance (baqa') in a state of existence, and this is not accepted by the Karramiyya, for they claim that the substance in the first state of its existence is described with endurance just as it is described with existence. And this opinion is held by 'Abbad al-Saymari, the companion of Hisham ibn 'Amr, from the group of the Mu'tazila. Thus al-Ka'bi related from him in al-Maqalat.

We say: Those who oppose us in the matter from the leaders of the Mu'tazila conceded to us this [premise] upon which we built, so we spoke with them on what passed based on their concession.

As for the Karramiyya and al-Saymari, we say to them: This from you is a denial of necessities and an ignorance of what is self-evident, and a breach of the consensus of all the people of language. For they allow themselves to say 'it existed and did not endure' and if endurance were attributable to the essence like existence, then the statement of one who says 'it existed and did not endure' would be like the statement of one who says 'it existed and did not exist'. And since this is considered a contradiction, unlike the first, it indicates the invalidity of this opinion, which is baseless and innovated.

Similarly, people say in supplication: 'May God preserve you' (abqaka Allah), and no one allows saying to another: 'May God bring you into existence' (awjadaka Allah). And if the two expressions were in reality referring to one thing, they would not refrain from using one of them universally [؟] while allowing the use of the other. Similarly, 'the enduring' (al-baqi) and 'the permanent' (al-da'im) are among synonymous expressions. Then consensus has occurred on the impossibility of using the term 'the permanent' (al-da'im), so likewise 'the enduring' (al-baqi).
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer concerning the attribute of endurance (baqa'). The opponent (Karramiyya and al-Saymari) objects that the author's previous inference wrongly presupposes that a substance cannot be described with endurance from the first moment, whereas they claim it is described with endurance just as with existence. The author responds by first noting that the leading Mu'tazila actually conceded the premise, so the earlier argument was based on their concession. As for the Karramiyya and al-Saymari, the author accuses them of denying self-evident truths (daruriyyat) and breaking the consensus of linguists. He gives two arguments: First, linguistically, people say 'it existed and did not endure' without contradiction, but if endurance were identical to existence, saying 'it existed and did not endure' would be like saying 'it existed and did not exist', which is a contradiction. Therefore endurance is distinct from existence. Second, people pray 'May God preserve you' (abqaka Allah) but do not say 'May God bring you into existence' (awjadaka Allah) for someone already existing. If the two expressions referred to the same thing, they would be used interchangeably. Moreover, the terms 'al-baqi' and 'al-da'im' are considered synonymous, and since consensus prohibits using 'al-da'im' for God (as it implies perpetuity by nature), the same applies to 'al-baqi'. Thus, baqa' cannot be an inherent attribute from the first moment.

Key Terms
البقاء
الكرامية
الصيمري
الضروريات
البداهة
إجماع أهل اللسان
الباقي
الدائم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqa' (endurance) is identical to existence and is present from the first moment of a thing's existence.
Correction: Baqa' is a distinct attribute that can be absent while existence remains, as shown by linguistic usage where 'it existed and did not endure' is not contradictory, unlike 'it existed and did not exist'.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that baqa' cannot be identical to existence?
A) Because people say 'it existed and did not endure' without contradiction.
B) Because existence is a necessary attribute of God.
C) Because the Karramiyya deny it.
D) Because al-Saymari was a Mu'tazili.

Key Takeaway
Baqa' (endurance) is a distinct attribute from existence, as shown by linguistic usage; it cannot be inherent from the first moment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage argues that denying the distinction between existence and endurance is a 'denial of self-evident truths' and a 'breach of the consensus of linguists.' Is there an area of your faith where you have ignored clear linguistic or rational evidence because it conflicted with your assumptions? What would it take for you to submit to that evidence today?
?
Consider the supplication 'abqaka Allah' (May God preserve you) — something you likely say without thinking. How does recognizing that endurance is a distinct gift from existence change the way you thank Allah for your continued life? Write down one specific blessing you experienced today that was not just your existence, but your ongoing preservation, and thank Allah for it.
?
Al-Nasafi uses ordinary language ('it existed and did not endure') to dismantle a theological error. When was the last time you allowed a simple, clear truth from the Qur'an or Sunnah to overturn a complicated opinion you held? What is holding you back from doing so right now?

Refutation of the Karramiyya on Baqa
Refutes the claim that substances have baqa from the beginning using linguistic consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and rational arguments that prove baqa (permanence) is not identical to existence and cannot be attributed to originated things from the beginning.

Core Idea
Language itself refutes the idea that permanence is identical to existence.

In this lesson, we examine a key refutation by Imam al-Nasafi against the Karramiyya and al-Saymari, who claimed that substances are described with baqa from the moment of existence. Using linguistic consensus and self-evident truths, the author demonstrates that baqa cannot be a concomitant of existence but is a separate attribute. The passage presents three crisp arguments from everyday language and logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing view
Read the beginning of the passage to understand what the Karramiyya and al-Saymari claim about baqa.
They claim that a substance (jawhar) is described with baqa from the first state of its existence, just as it is described with existence.
2
Analyze the contradiction test
The author argues that if baqa were identical to existence, 'existed and did not remain' would be as contradictory as 'existed and did not exist'. Notice why the first is not considered contradictory.
This shows that baqa is not identical to existence.
3
Examine the supplication argument
Consider the difference between 'abqāka Allāh' and 'awjadaka Allāh'. Why do people use one but not the other?
If baqa and existence were the same, both phrases would be used interchangeably.
4
Understand the synonymity argument
Learn how the author connects 'bāqī' and 'dā'im' and uses consensus on 'dā'im' to rule out 'bāqī' for originated things.
This reinforces that baqa cannot be applied to created beings from the beginning.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Synthesize the three arguments to see how they collectively refute the Karramiyya position.
The author uses linguistic consensus (ijmā') as a decisive proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حالة الوجود ، وهذا غير مسلم عند الكرامية فإنهم يزعمون أن الجوهر في أول أحوال وجوده موصوفا بالبقاء كما هو موصوف بالوجود، وإلى هذا القول يذهب عباد الصيمري صاحب هشام بن عمرو من جملة المعتزلة، كذا حكى عنه الكعبي في المقالات. قلنا: إن المخالفين لنا في المسألة من رؤساء المعتزلة سلموا لنا هذا الذي بنينا فتكلمنا على ما مر معهم بناء على تسليمهم. فأما الكرامية والصيمري فإنا نقول لهم: هذا منكم جحد الضروريات وإنكار البداهة، وخرق إجماع أهل اللسان قاطبة، فإنهم يستجيزون أن يقولوا وجد كذا ولم يبق ولو كان البقاء راجعًا إلى الذات كالوجود لكان قول القائل وجد ولم يبق كقول القائل وجد ولم يوجد وحيث عد هذا تناقضا دون الأول، دل على بطلان هذا الرأي المستنزل المحدث. وكذا الناس يقولون في الدعاء : أبقاك الله، ولا يستجيز أحد أن يقول لآخر : أوجدك الله، ولو كان اللفظان في الحقيقة راجعين إلى شيء واحد لما امتنعوا عن إطلاق أحدهما مع الإطباق على إجازة إطلاق الآخر، وكذا الباقي والدائم من جملة الألفاظ المترادفة، ثم انعقد الإجماع على استحالة إطلاق لفظ الدائم فكذا الباقي.
The state of existence, and this is not conceded by the Karramiyya, for they claim that the substance (jawhar) in the first state of its existence is described with permanence (baqā') just as it is described with existence. And this opinion is held by 'Ubad al-Ṣaymarī, the companion of Hishām ibn 'Amr from among the Mu'tazila; thus al-Ka'bī reported from him in al-Maqālāt. We said: Those who oppose us among the leaders of the Mu'tazila conceded to us this upon which we built; so we spoke with them based on their concession. As for the Karramiyya and al-Ṣaymarī, we say to them: This from you is a denial of necessities and a rejection of self-evident truths, and a breaking of the consensus of all people of language entirely. For they permit themselves to say 'something existed and did not remain'. If permanence were referable to the essence like existence, then the statement of one who says 'it existed and did not remain' would be like the statement of one who says 'it existed and did not exist'. And since this is considered a contradiction while the former is not, this indicates the invalidity of this novel and baseless opinion. Similarly, people say in supplication: 'May God keep you' (abqāka Allāh), and no one permits himself to say to another: 'May God bring you into existence' (awjadaka Allāh). If the two words were in reality referable to one thing, they would not refrain from using one of them while agreeing to permit the use of the other. Likewise, 'the permanent' (al-bāqī) and 'the eternal' (al-dā'im) are among synonymous terms. Then consensus has been established on the impossibility of using the term 'the eternal' [for originated things]; similarly 'the permanent'.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. The author begins by stating the opposing position: the Karramiyya claim that a substance (jawhar) is described with permanence (baqā') from the very first state of its existence, just as it is described with existence. This view is also attributed to 'Ubad al-Ṣaymarī of the Mu'tazila. The author then explains that the leaders of the Mu'tazila who opposed him had conceded the point on which he built his argument, so his discussion with them was based on that concession. But the Karramiyya and al-Ṣaymarī have not conceded; therefore, he addresses them directly. He accuses them of denying self-evident truths and breaking the consensus of Arabic speakers. His first argument: if permanence were identical to existence, then saying 'it existed and did not remain' would be as contradictory as saying 'it existed and did not exist'. But speakers do not consider the former a contradiction, only the latter, proving that permanence is not identical to existence. Second, people say 'abqāka Allāh' (may God keep you) but never say 'awjadaka Allāh' (may God bring you into existence); if the two words were equivalent, they would use them interchangeably. Third, 'al-bāqī' and 'al-dā'im' are synonyms, and consensus holds that 'al-dā'im' cannot be applied to originated things, so 'al-bāqī' also cannot be applied in that sense. Thus the opponents' claim that an accident or substance is 'bāqī' from the beginning is linguistically invalid.

جوهر (jawhar)
كرامية (Karramiyya)
صيمري (Ṣaymarī)
إجماع (ijmā')
ضروريات (ḍarūriyyāt)
بداهة (badāha)
دائم (dā'im)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqa is an inherent attribute of substances from the moment of creation, just like existence.
Correction: Linguistic evidence shows that baqa is distinct from existence: one can say 'existed and did not remain' without contradiction, and supplication uses 'abqāka' but not 'awjadaka'.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument using the supplication 'abqāka Allāh' versus 'awjadaka Allāh'?
A) Both phrases are used interchangeably in Arabic.
B) People say 'abqāka Allāh' but not 'awjadaka Allāh', proving that baqā' is not identical to existence.
C) 'Awjadaka Allāh' is more common than 'abqāka Allāh'.
D) The author rejects both phrases as innovations.

Key Takeaway
Permanence (baqa) is not identical to existence; it is a separate attribute that cannot be predicated of originated things from the beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray 'abqāka Allāh' for someone, do you realize that their very continued existence is a gift from Allah separate from their initial creation? How does this affect your gratitude for each moment of life?
?
The author says that denying the distinction between existence and permanence is 'a denial of necessities and a rejection of self-evident truths'. Are there areas of your own faith where you ignore clear truths because they conflict with your desires or comfort?
?
If permanence is not inherent in anything but Allah, what does that mean for your attachments to worldly things? Can you truly say you rely on Allah alone for your 'continuance' in this life and the next? What would change if you lived with that awareness today?

Proof that Baqa is an Added Attribute and Refutation of Objections
Proof, objection, and refutation regarding baqa as an added attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why baqa must be a distinct attribute added to the essence, and how the author refutes the objection that God's permanence prevents contraries because of power limitations.

Core Idea
Permanence cannot be essential to a contingent; otherwise it would become necessary like God.

This passage presents a key argument in the debate over divine attributes. The author first proves that permanence (baqa) cannot be an essential property of contingent beings, then answers an objection from the Mu'tazilites, particularly al-Jubbā'ī. By the end, you'll see how the argument clarifies the nature of God's necessary existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main proof
Read the first part of the passage that states the conditional: if a thing were permanent by itself, its existence would be necessary after origination. Notice the consequence.
The author uses the term 'bāqī' for the permanent thing.
2
Understand the analogy with God
The author compares a necessary existent like God, who cannot have a contrary. See how this supports the conclusion that permanence is added.
God's permanence is essential, but for contingents it cannot be.
3
Examine the objection
The objector claims that God's lack of contrary is due to impossibility of a contrary being within power, not due to necessary existence.
This is an attempt to break the analogy.
4
Follow the author's answer
The author flips the argument: it's actually the necessity of permanence that prevents a contrary, and then uses the objection to refute al-Jubbā'ī's own theory of annihilation.
The refutation targets the Mu'tazilī doctrine of accidents and substances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه وبطلان ما ذهب إليه الخصوم أن الباقي لو كان باقيًا لنفسه أو لا لمعنى أكثر من ذاته لكان وجوده واجبًا بعد حدوثه؛ لأن كونه باقيًا من مقتضيات ذاته، وما وجب وجوده لم ينتف بحدوث ضده كالقديم سبحانه وتعالى لما وجب وجوده في كل حال لا يحدث فيه ضده لم يصح أن يكون له ضد يوجب عدمه. فإن قيل : إنما استحال عدم القديم لوجود ضده لاستحالة كون الضد مقدوراً عليه؛ لأن ما لم يكن مقدوراً في نفسه لم يكن له ضد يوصف به. قلنا لهم : إنما استحال أن يكون له ضد مقدور عليه لقادر لوجوب بقائه لولا ذلك لتصور وجود ضده، وهذا منا إلزام على الجبائي وابنه؛ إذ من مذهبهما أن عدم الأعراض بطريان أضدادهما عليهما وعدم الجواهر بإيجاد الله تعالى الفناء لا في محل وهو عرض مناف مضاد لجميع الجواهر فتفنى الجواهر لوجود ضدها، ولا تفنى الجواهر ما لم يوجد الفناء المضاد لها، ولهذا أنكرا قدرة الله تعالى - تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون المبطلون علوا كبيرًا على إفناء بعض الأجسام والجواهر مع بقاء بعضها، لأن الفناء لو لم يوجد لها لما تصور عدم جوهر ما، ولو وجد لكان ضد الجميع فيفنى الجميع.
And it indicates the correctness of what we have held and the invalidity of what the opponents have held, that if the permanent thing (al-bāqī) were permanent by itself or with no meaning more than its essence, its existence would be necessary after its origination; because its being permanent is a requirement of its essence. And that whose existence is necessary is not removed by the occurrence of its contrary, like the Eternal (al-Qadīm), may He be exalted, since His existence is necessary in every state, no contrary occurs in Him, it is not valid for Him to have a contrary that would necessitate His non-existence. If it is said: The impossibility of the non-existence of the Eternal due to the existence of a contrary is because it is impossible for the contrary to be within power; because what is not possible in itself cannot have a contrary described by it. We say to them: It is impossible for Him to have a contrary that is within the power of a powerful agent because of the necessity of His permanence; otherwise, the existence of a contrary would be conceivable. And this from us is an imposition against al-Jubbā'ī and his son; for their doctrine is that the non-existence of accidents occurs by the arrival of their contraries upon them, and the non-existence of substances occurs by God's creation of annihilation (fanā') in no locus, which is a contrary opposed to all substances. Thus substances cease to exist due to the existence of their contrary, and substances do not cease as long as the annihilation that is contrary to them does not exist. For this reason they denied the power of God—exalted is God above what the wrongdoers and falsifiers say, with great exaltation—to annihilate some bodies and substances while leaving some of them, because if annihilation did not exist for them, no substance could be conceived to cease, and if it existed, it would be contrary to all and would annihilate all.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a proof followed by an objection and its answer. The author first presents his proof: if a thing were permanent by itself (i.e., without an added attribute of permanence), then its existence would become necessary after it comes into existence, because permanence would be a necessary consequence of its essence. But a necessary existent cannot be removed by the occurrence of a contrary, as is the case with God the Eternal. Therefore, a contingent thing cannot have its permanence as a necessary consequence of its essence; hence permanence must be an added attribute. The objector then raises a point: the impossibility of non-existence for the Eternal is due to the impossibility of a contrary being within power, because what is not possible in itself cannot have a contrary. The author answers: the impossibility of a contrary for God is due to the necessity of His permanence; otherwise, a contrary would be conceivable. He then turns this into a refutation against al-Jubbā'ī and his son, who hold that accidents cease by the arrival of their contraries and substances cease by God's creation of annihilation (fanā') in a non-locus, which is a contrary to all substances. The author argues that on their view, if annihilation did not exist for a substance, it could never cease, and if it existed, it would annihilate all substances simultaneously. Thus they are forced to deny God's power to annihilate some substances while leaving others, which is an absurd consequence.

Key Terms
باقي (bāqī)
بقاء (baqā')
قديم (qadīm)
ضد (ḍidd)
فناء (fanā')
جبائي (al-Jubbā'ī)
عرض ('araḍ)
جوهر (jawhar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the impossibility of God having a contrary is due to lack of power, but the author clarifies it is due to the necessity of His permanence.
Correction: The author argues that God's permanence is necessary, and that is the primary reason a contrary is impossible; the power argument is secondary.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what would follow if a contingent thing were permanent by its essence?
A) It would be impossible for it to cease to exist.
B) Its existence would be necessary after its origination.
C) It would be subject to change by a contrary.
D) It would be eternal like God.

Key Takeaway
Baqa must be a distinct attribute because if it were essential, the thing would become necessarily existent, which contradicts the contingent nature of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your very existence and continued existence are gifts from Allah, not inherent to you? When was the last time you acted as if you had the power to sustain yourself, forgetting that you are contingent every moment?
?
The opponents denied God’s power to annihilate selectively because their logic forced them. Are there any theological beliefs you hold that, if followed consistently, would limit God’s omnipotence? Are you willing to accept paradoxes in faith rather than rational constraints?
?
If your permanence is not essential but a gift, how does that change your attitude toward your life, possessions, and relationships? Will you start today to recite 'Ya Hayyu Ya Qayyum' with the understanding that your existence is constantly sustained by the Eternal?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
God's Necessary Existence Cannot Be Negated by a Contrary
Author states God's necessary existence; then objection and answer regarding impossibility of a contrary for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's necessary existence cannot be negated by a contrary, and how the author uses an entailment to refute the Mu'tazilite doctrine of annihilation.

Core Idea
God's endurance is necessary; no contrary can negate Him.

The author begins by affirming that God's attribute of endurance (baqa') is an intrinsic necessity of His essence. He then anticipates a Mu'tazilite objection concerning the impossibility of a contrary for God. The answer not only refutes the objection but turns into a powerful entailment against the Mu'tazilite theory of annihilation (fana'), exposing an internal inconsistency in their system.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial claim
Read the first line: 'كونه باقيًا من مقتضيات ذاته' and the following statement about the impossibility of a contrary negating God's existence.
Notice the logical structure: what has necessary existence cannot be negated by a contrary.
2
Identify the objection and answer
Find where the opponent objects (فإن قيل) and the author's response (قلنا لهم). Understand how the author turns the objection on its head.
The objection claims contraries only apply to things within power; the answer shows that God's necessary endurance precludes any contrary.
3
Follow the entailment against al-Jubba'i
Read the section beginning with 'وهذا منا إلزام على الجبائي وابنه'. See how the author applies the Mu'tazilites' own principles to prove a contradiction.
The Mu'tazilites believe annihilation (fana') is a contrary to all substances, so if it exists, all are annihilated, negating selective annihilation.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the author uses logical entailment (ilzam) to show that the Mu'tazilite position leads to absurdity, thereby defending God's necessary endurance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كونه باقيًا من مقتضيات ذاته، وما وجب وجوده لم ينتف بحدوث ضده كالقديم سبحانه وتعالى لما وجب وجوده في كل حال لا يحدث فيه ضده لم يصح أن يكون له ضد يوجب عدمه. فإن قيل : إنما استحال عدم القديم لوجود ضده لاستحالة كون الضد مقدوراً عليه؛ لأن ما لم يكن مقدوراً في نفسه لم يكن له ضد يوصف به. قلنا لهم : إنما استحال أن يكون له ضد مقدور عليه لقادر لوجوب بقائه لولا ذلك لتصور وجود ضده، وهذا منا إلزام على الجبائي وابنه؛ إذ من مذهبهما أن عدم الأعراض بطريان أضدادهما عليهما وعدم الجواهر بإيجاد الله تعالى الفناء لا في محل وهو عرض مناف مضاد لجميع الجواهر فتفنى الجواهر لوجود ضدها، ولا تفنى الجواهر ما لم يوجد الفناء المضاد لها، ولهذا أنكرا قدرة الله تعالى - تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون المبطلون علوا كبيرًا على إفناء بعض الأجسام والجواهر مع بقاء بعضها، لأن الفناء لو لم يوجد لها لما تصور عدم جوهر ما، ولو وجد لكان ضد الجميع فيفنى الجميع.
The fact that He is enduring is from the necessities of His essence, and what has necessary existence is not negated by the occurrence of a contrary, like the Eternal (al-Qadim), the Exalted, for when His existence is necessary in every state, no contrary occurs in Him, so it cannot be that He has a contrary that would necessitate His non-existence. For if it is said: 'The non-existence of the Eternal is impossible due to the existence of a contrary only because it is impossible that the contrary be [within] power; because what is not within power in itself has no contrary attributed to it.' We say to them: Rather, it is impossible that He have a contrary that is within power for a powerful being because of the necessity of His endurance, otherwise the existence of His contrary would be conceivable. And this from us is an entailment (ilzam) upon al-Jubba'i and his son; for from their doctrine is that the non-existence of accidents is by the incidence of their contraries upon them, and the non-existence of substances is by God's creation of annihilation (fana') not in a locus, which is a contrary accident opposed to all substances, so the substances cease to exist due to the existence of their contrary, and the substances do not cease to exist unless the annihilation contrary to them exists. And for this reason they denied God's power—exalted is God above what the unjust and false say, greatly exalted—over annihilating some bodies and substances while leaving others, because if annihilation did not exist for them, non-existence of any substance would not be conceivable, and if it existed, it would be contrary to all, so it would annihilate all.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage begins with a statement about God's attribute of endurance (baqa'): that it is from the necessities of His essence, meaning His existence is necessary and cannot be negated by the occurrence of any contrary. The author then raises an objection from an opponent: the opponent argues that the impossibility of God's non-existence due to a contrary is only because the contrary would have to be within God's power—but since God cannot be subject to power, a contrary cannot be attributed to Him. The author answers by clarifying that the impossibility of God having a contrary that is subject to another's power is due to His necessary endurance, otherwise such a contrary could exist. Then the author turns this into an entailment against al-Jubba'i and his son (the Mu'tazilite leaders). He explains their position: they hold that accidents cease to exist by the incidence of their contraries, and substances cease to exist by God's creation of 'annihilation' (fana') not in a locus, which is an accident opposed to all substances. Therefore, according to them, if annihilation exists, it annihilates all substances at once, which leads to the denial that God can selectively annihilate some substances while leaving others. The author uses this to show a contradiction in their own principles.

Key Terms
باقٍ (al-bāqī: enduring)
ضد (ḍidd: contrary)
قديم (al-qadīm: the Eternal)
فناء (fanā': annihilation)
إلزام (ilzām: entailment/forced implication)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the objection is about God being subject to change, but the focus is logical impossibility of a contrary being in power.
Correction: The objection actually argues that a contrary can only apply to something within power, and since God is not within power, no contrary exists. The author corrects that the impossibility stems from God's necessary endurance.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why can God not have a contrary that is within power for a powerful being?
A) Because God is not within power, so no contrary applies.
B) Because God's endurance is necessary, so existence of such a contrary is inconceivable.
C) Because contraries only exist in accidents.
D) Because God has no attributes.

Key Takeaway
God's necessary endurance precludes any contrary, and the Mu'tazilite theory of annihilation leads to the absurdity of universal annihilation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's existence is so necessary that nothing—not your doubts, not your sins, not any circumstance—can ever negate His reality? How does this belief shape your response to moments when you feel distant from Him?
?
The Mu'tazilites denied God's power over selective annihilation, limiting Him by their own reasoning. Have you ever, in your heart, imposed limits on God based on your understanding? What does this lesson teach you about submitting to God's absolute power?
?
If God's endurance is necessary and yours is entirely contingent, what does that mean for how you view your own life and struggles? Are you living as if your existence depends on Him alone? What one thing will you change today to reflect that dependency?

The Conditional Proof: Why Endurance Must Be an Additional Attribute
Author presents conditional proof and classifies views on annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi proof that endurance (baqa') is an additional attribute distinct from the divine essence, based on the impossibility of an accident ceasing to exist if it were essential.

Core Idea
If endurance were essential, nothing would ever cease to exist.

To establish that endurance is an additional attribute of Allah, the author presents a powerful conditional argument: if endurance were identical to the essence, then anything that endures would do so necessarily and could never cease to exist. Since we observe that created accidents (like colors) do cease, endurance cannot be essential. He then examines all possible explanations for how a thing ceases to exist, showing that each fails for accidents, thus reinforcing the need for an added attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditional proof
Read the opening conditional statement carefully. Understand that the argument hinges on the impossibility of an accident ceasing to exist if it were enduring by itself.
Note that 'accident' here means any non-essential property of a body.
2
Examine the four possibilities for cessation
The author lists four ways a thing could cease: (1) creation of an opposite, (2) cutting off endurance, (3) cutting off colors/modes, (4) incidence of a contrary. Notice which schools each view belongs to.
The third view only applies to bodies, not accidents.
3
Understand why accidents cannot cease by any of these
The author argues that for accidents, options (1) and (2) are impossible because accidents cannot receive another accident; option (3) is only for bodies; and option (4) is logically impossible as will be shown. Thus, the only consistent explanation is that endurance is an additional attribute that can be removed.
This sets up the need for the later detailed refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه أن البقاء لو لم يكن معنى زائدًا على الذات وكان الباقي باقيًا لذاته ، وكان العرض باقيًا لذاته لما تصور عدمه، لأن عدمه لا يخلو إما أن يكون يخلق منافيه فينعدم في الثاني من خلق الفناء فيه كما ذهب إليه محمد بن شبيب وأبو العباس القلانسى وكثير من المتكلمين، وهو اختيار الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدي في عدم الأجسام وهذا محال في الأعراض، لأنها لا تقبل عرضا آخر ليوجد فيها الفناء، وإما أن تكون بقطع البقاء عنه فينعدم في الثاني كما هو مذهب ضرار بن عمرو، وهو اختيار أبي الحسن الأشعري وأبي القاسم الكعبي، فإن من مذهب هؤلاء أن البقاء عرض حادث في الأجسام لا يبقى بنفسه بل يتجدد ساعة فساعة ، فإذا أراد الله تعالى إفناء الجسم قطع عنه البقاء فلم يخلقه فيه فينعدم، والعرض ليس بمحل لخلق البقاء فيه ليقال إنه إذا لم يخلق فيه البقاء في الثاني انعدم، فلم يتصور الفناء بهذا الطريق على مذهب هؤلاء، وأما أن يكون يقطع الألوان والأكوان كما ذهب إليه أبو بكر الباقلاني من متأخري متكلمي أهل الحديث؛ لأن هذا لن يتصور إلا في الأجسام التي يحلها الألوان والأكوان وأما أن يكون بطريان ضده عليه بأن يطرأ عليه ضده فيعدمه وهذا هو مذهب هؤلاء المخالفين لنا من المعتزلة في المسألة وهذا محال، لأن هذا الضد القائم الثابت المتقرر في المحل ليس بأولى بالعدم من الضد الطارئ الحادث آنفًا، ولا معنى لقول بعض أغبيائهم : إن الحدوث أقوى من البقاء ؛ لأن هذا ليس بأولى ممن يقول : البقاء أقوى من الحدوث. ثم الدليل على أن الباقي أقوى من الحادث في الوجود أن الباقي لم يتعلق وجوده بقدرة يصح منع القادر منه ويتوهم ذلك فيه، والحدث يتعلق وجوده بقدرة يصح منع القادر منه ويتوهم ذلك في الجملة، والدليل عليه أن الباقي واجب الوجود في حال طريان ضده عليه، والحادث جائز الوجود في حال حدوثه، ولا شك أن واجب الوجود أقوى في الوجود من جائز الوجود، على أن قوته ليس بأكثر من وجوده، ولا وجود للحادث قبل حالة الحدوث، فعدمه قبل حدوثه لا يكون موجبًا قوته في وجوده، والباقي له وجود قبل وجوده في هذه الحالة التي حدث فيه الضد فوجوده قبل وجوده موجب قوته في وجوده، والذي يقرأ هذا أن العرض الحادث
And what indicates the correctness of what we have gone to is that if endurance (al-baqa') were not an additional meaning over the essence, and the enduring were enduring by itself, and the accident were enduring by itself, its non-existence would not be conceivable. For its non-existence does not go beyond: either that its opposite (munafi) is created so that it ceases to exist in the second [moment] from the creation of annihilation in it, as held by Muhammad ibn Shabib, Abu al-'Abbas al-Qalanisi, and many theologians, and it is the choice of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi regarding the non-existence of bodies—and this is impossible in accidents because they do not accept another accident in which annihilation may be created; or that endurance is cut off from it so that it ceases to exist in the second [moment], as is the doctrine of Dirar ibn 'Amr, and it is the choice of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu al-Qasim al-Ka'bi, for among the doctrine of these is that endurance is a newly occurring accident (hadith) in bodies, not lasting by itself but renewing moment by moment. So when God wishes to annihilate a body, He cuts off endurance from it, not creating it in it, so it ceases to exist. And the accident is not a locus for creating endurance in it to say that if He does not create endurance in it in the second [moment], it ceases to exist, so annihilation is not conceivable by this method according to the doctrine of these. Or that He cuts off colors and modes (akwan) as held by Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, from the later theologians of the people of hadith, for this is only conceivable in bodies that admit colors and modes. Or that it is by the incidence of its contrary upon it, that its contrary attacks it and annihilates it—and this is the doctrine of these opponents of ours, the Mu'tazila, in this matter, and this is impossible, because this contrary that is established, fixed, and settled in the locus is not more worthy of non-existence than the attacking contrary that newly occurs, nor is there meaning in the saying of some of their ignorant ones: 'that the newly occurring is stronger than endurance', because this is not more worthy than one who says: 'endurance is stronger than the newly occurring.' Then the evidence that the enduring (al-baqi) is stronger in existence than the newly occurring (al-hadith) is that the existence of the enduring is not attached to a power that the powerful one could withhold and that conceivably be prevented, while the existence of the newly occurring is attached to a power that the powerful one could withhold and that conceivably be prevented in general. And the evidence for this is that the enduring is necessary of existence (wajib al-wujud) in the state of the incidence of its contrary upon it, while the newly occurring is contingent of existence (ja'iz al-wujud) in the state of its occurrence. And there is no doubt that the necessary of existence is stronger in existence than the contingent of existence, and its strength is not more than its existence. And there is no existence for the newly occurring before the state of its occurrence, so its non-existence before its occurrence does not cause strength in its existence. And the enduring has existence before its existence in this state in which the contrary occurred to it, so its existence before its existence causes strength in its existence. And he who reads this [will recognize that the newly occurring accident...]
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage begins with a proof that endurance (baqa') is an additional attribute separate from the essence. The author argues: if endurance were not something added to the essence, then an accident (like a color) that endures would do so by itself, and would never be able to cease to exist. But accidents do cease, so endurance must be additional. Then he classifies the various positions on how a thing ceases to exist, presenting four views: (1) Creation of an opposite (like fana') in the thing—impossible for accidents. (2) Cutting off endurance—held by Dirar, Ash'ari, and Ka'bi, but this requires that endurance be created in bodies, not in accidents. (3) Cutting off colors and modes—held by al-Baqillani, only applicable to bodies. (4) Incidence of a contrary—the Mu'tazilite view. The author refutes (4) by arguing that if a pre-existing contrary is stable, it is no more deserving of non-existence than the newly arriving contrary; thus the Mu'tazilite argument is arbitrary. Then he provides a further proof that the state of being enduring is stronger in existence than being newly occurring. The enduring's existence is not dependent on a power that can be withheld, while the newly occurring's existence is contingent on power. Also, the enduring is necessary (wajib) in that state, whereas the newly occurring is contingent (ja'iz). The author also points out that the enduring had existence before the state of the striking contrary, which gives it strength, while the newly occurring had no prior existence. The passage ends with an incomplete sentence about the newly occurring accident.

Key Terms
بقاء (baqa': endurance)
معنى زائد (ma'na za'id: additional meaning/attribute)
فناء (fana': annihilation)
حادث (hadith: newly occurring)
باقي (baqi: enduring)
ضد (didd: contrary)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Mu'tazilite view of annihilation by a contrary is logically sound.
Correction: The author shows it leads to an arbitrary selection between two contraries, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the view that annihilation occurs by creating an opposite impossible for accidents?
A) Because accidents cannot have opposites.
B) Because accidents cannot receive another accident.
C) Because only God can create opposites.
D) Because opposites are eternal.

Key Takeaway
The conditional proof and classification demonstrate that only the Maturidi view—that endurance is an additional attribute—accounts for the fact that accidents cease to exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The conditional proof shows that if endurance were essential to you, you would never cease to exist. But you know you will, and your existence is a gift from Allah every moment. How does this realization change the way you value the time you have right now? What would you do today if you truly lived knowing that your endurance is not by your own essence?
?
The author refutes many views on how things pass away, each failing to explain the cessation of an accident. Among those views, perhaps you have unconsciously adopted the idea that things simply 'end' naturally. But this lesson teaches that cessation requires a specific act of the Creator. How does this truth affect the way you view the temporary things in your life? Are you holding onto something as if it will last forever, when in reality its continuation is a gift being renewed every instant?
?
The Mu'tazilite view of annihilation by a contrary was dismissed because one contrary is no more deserving of existence than another. In your own life, when you face conflicting desires, do you assume that one should naturally overcome the other? How does this lesson challenge your assumption about how change occurs, and remind you that only Allah's will brings about change?
