The Obligation of Hajj and Jihad Depends on First Ability
Nasafi argues that commands rely on istita'a al-ula, not immediate ability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Islamic theology, the command to perform an act (taklif) is based on the first ability (istita'a al-ula) to fulfil it, not on the immediate ability at the time of action, and how this principle is demonstrated through the examples of Hajj and jihad.

Core Idea
Command depends on first ability, not immediate ability.

Imam Nasafi tackles a fundamental question in usul al-fiqh: when does an obligation become binding? Is it when you already have the ability to perform the act, or when you have the potential to acquire the means? In this passage, he argues firmly for the latter—the 'first ability'—and supports it with examples from Hajj and jihad, as well as a rational principle and a scriptural proof from the story of Moses and al-Khidr. Let's unpack his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Notice the examples and the logical structure.
2
Identify the two examples
Find where Nasafi gives examples of Hajj and jihad. How does each example show that obligation exists even when immediate ability is lacking?
Example 1: person in Bukhara with provision and mount. Example 2: Muslims at edges of Islam against distant enemies.
3
Understand the principle
Nasafi states that command to an act is command to its prerequisites. This is the core rational principle. How does it connect to the examples?
4
Analyze the rejection of the alternative
The passage refutes the idea that one must first acquire ability before obligation. Understand why Nasafi considers this an inversion of reason.
He argues it confuses the relationship between obligation and its conditions.
5
Examine the proof from Moses
The story of Moses and al-Khidr illustrates that the address depends on first ability. Why was Moses rebuked despite lacking immediate patience?
Because the means of patience were present; the lack was in the reality of patience, not the first ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غناء يشترطوا حقيقة القدرة، والصحيح ما ذهبنا إليه لما مر من الدلائل المعقولة، وقد ورد كتاب الله تعالى بتقرير ذلك، فإنه تعالى خاطب من ببخارى - عند وجود الزاد والراحلة وتوفر الأسباب والآلات - بأداء الحج وأوجب عليه ذلك، وإن كانت قدرة أداء أفعال الحج منعدمة ببخارى، وأوجب - عند عموم التغير وقصور من بالثغور من أهل الإسلام عن مقاومة من بإزائهم من الكفرة وعجزهم عن الذب عن البيضة وحماية الحوزة - على من بأطراف دار الإسلام من المسلمين الذين بهم وكفاية، جهاد أولئك الأعداء وذبهم عن حريم دار الإسلام، وإن كانت قدرة مجاهدة العدو بأقصى الروم والهند منعدمة. ولا شك أن الحج والجهاد يجبان أولاً، ثم لما لم يتمكن من أدائهما إلا بقطع المسافة وجب عليه ذلك. والخروج على ما هو الأصل أن الأمر بالفعل أمر به وبما لم يتوصل إلى أدائه إلا به، ولا وجه إلى القول بأنه يجب عليه الخروج وقطع المسافة ليحصل له قدرة الأداء ثم يجب الأداء حينئذ لأن إيجاب تحصيل شرائط الأداء ثابت لما هو من ضرورة الخروج عن الواجب، فأما إيجاب تحصيل أسباب الوجوب أو شرائطه فغير ثابت البتة لما في الأول لاتباع التابع المتبوع وفي الثاني اتباع المتبوع التابع، وهو قلب المعقول – يدل عليه أن من وجد الزاد والراحلة ولم يخرج إلى الحج حتى مات يأثم إثم ترك الحج بإجماع الأمة لا إثم ترك الخروج وصاحب موسى عليه السلام عاتبه عند ترك الصبر مع قوله: إنك لن تستطيع معي صبرا لما أن أسباب الصبر وآلاته كانت ثابتة، وإنما المنعدم حقيقة استطاعة الصبر، دل أن الخطاب يعتمد الاستطاعة الأولى لا الثانية.
Sufficiency? They condition the reality of power, and the correct is what we have held due to the rational proofs that have passed. And the Book of Allah has come establishing that. Indeed, He addressed the one in Bukhara – when provision and mount existed and means and instruments were available – to perform Hajj and made it obligatory upon him, even though the power to perform the acts of Hajj was nonexistent in Bukhara. And He made obligatory – at the time of general change and the insufficiency of those at the frontiers among the people of Islam to resist those facing them from the disbelievers, and their inability to defend the community and protect the territory – upon those at the edges of the abode of Islam among the Muslims who have sufficiency, the jihad against those enemies and repelling them from the sanctum of the abode of Islam, even though the power to fight the enemy at the farthest reaches of Rome and India was nonexistent. There is no doubt that Hajj and jihad are obligatory first, then when he cannot perform them except by traversing the distance, that becomes obligatory upon him. And the correct principle is that command to an act is a command to it and to that without which the act cannot be performed. There is no consideration for the saying that it is obligatory upon him to go out and traverse the distance to acquire the power of performance, then performance becomes obligatory then, because the obligation of acquiring the conditions of performance is established as a necessary consequence of fulfilling the obligation. As for the obligation of acquiring the causes or conditions of obligation itself, it is not established at all, because in the first the follower follows the followed, and in the second the followed follows the follower, which is an inversion of reason. This is indicated by the fact that whoever has provision and mount and does not go out for Hajj until he dies, he sins for abandoning Hajj by consensus, not for abandoning travel. And the companion of Moses (peace be upon him) was rebuked when he abandoned patience despite His saying: 'Indeed, you will never be able to be patient with me,' because the causes and instruments of patience were present, and what was absent was the reality of the capacity for patience. This indicates that the address depends on the first capacity, not the second.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage argues that the command to perform an act (like Hajj or jihad) does not require that the person already possesses the immediate ability to perform the act in his current location. Rather, the obligation arises based on the first ability (istita'a al-ula), which is the potential to acquire the means to perform the act. The text gives examples: Allah commands Hajj upon a person in Bukhara who has provision and mount, even though he cannot physically perform the Hajj rituals in Bukhara. Similarly, Allah commands jihad upon Muslims in distant lands against enemies far away, even though they cannot fight them immediately. The argument is that the command itself includes the obligation to undertake what is necessary to fulfill it, such as traveling. The alternative view—that the person must first acquire ability through travel and then the act becomes obligatory—is rejected because it confuses the relationship between the obligation and its conditions. The proof is that if someone dies without performing Hajj despite having provision and mount, he is sinful for abandoning Hajj, not for abandoning travel. The story of Moses and al-Khidr illustrates: Moses was rebuked for lacking patience despite the means of patience being present, showing that the command depends on the primary capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Obligation requires immediate ability to perform the act at the time of command.
Correction: Obligation is based on the first ability, i.e., having the means to acquire the ability, not on already possessing it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the address of command depend on?
A) The first ability (istita'a al-ula)
B) The immediate ability at the time of action
C) The presence of the act
D) The absence of obstacles

Key Takeaway
The address of divine command depends on the first ability, not the second, as shown by the obligations of Hajj and jihad and the story of Moses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a religious duty you have delayed because you felt you weren't ready or capable. According to this lesson, is that delay justified? What first ability (means, resources, health) have you already been given to fulfill it, and what step have you been avoiding because it feels distant?
?
You have the mount and provision—like the person in Bukhara who was obligated for Hajj. In your life, what 'mount and provision'—knowledge, time, influence—has Allah given you that you are using as an excuse not to act? What would it mean to take the first step today, even if the final goal seems far?
?
Moses had the means of patience but was still rebuked for not being patient. Where in your life have you blamed your circumstances ('I can't do this because...') when, in truth, you had everything you needed to start? Will you continue to excuse yourself, or will you accept the full weight of the command already upon you?

Divine Power: Invention vs. Acquisition
Nasafi states the Maturidi position on divine power as invention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction that divine power is for invention (ikhtira'), which uniquely affects both non-existence and existence at the moment of origination, contrasting with human power which is merely acquisition.

Core Idea
Divine power creates from nothing; human power only acquires.

Imam al-Nasafi introduces a key Maturidi principle: Allah's power is characterized as invention (ikhtira'), which uniquely affects both non-existence and existence at the moment of creation. This distinguishes divine power from human power, which is merely acquisition (kasb). Let's examine this foundational statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms: قدرة الباري and اختراع.
The passage is a single sentence but packed with meaning.
2
Understand the condition of ikhtira'
The condition states that the inventor's power must affect both non-existence and existence at the moment of origination. This is unique to divine power.
This implies that human power cannot affect non-existence.
3
Contrast with human power
Human power (qudrat al-kasb) is for acquisition, meaning it only affects existence, not non-existence. This is a key difference.
The passage sets up this contrast implicitly.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Think about why this distinction matters: it safeguards Allah's uniqueness as Creator and clarifies the nature of human agency.
This aligns with the Maturidi emphasis on tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكثير من أصحابنا يقولون بأن قدرة الباري جل جلاله متعلقة بالاختراع ومن شرط الاختراع أن تؤثر قدرة المخترع في العدم والوجود جميعًا حال حدوث
And many of our companions say that the power of the Exalted Creator is connected to invention (ikhtira'), and one condition of invention is that the power of the inventor affects non-existence and existence both at the moment of origination.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage introduces a classification: divine power (qudrat al-Bari) is related to invention (ikhtira'), meaning it creates from nothing. A condition of invention is that the power of the inventor simultaneously affects both non-existence and existence at the moment of origination. In contrast, human power (qudrat al-kasb) is for acquisition, which is concomitant with the act, not prior. This is a key Maturidi distinction.

D) The power is not needed for invention

Key Takeaway
Divine power, unlike human power, directly creates from nothing by affecting both non-existence and existence at the moment of origination.

Simultaneity of Power and Act in Maturidi Kalam
Nasafi argues that created power and act are simultaneous, not sequential.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidis hold that created power and the act occur simultaneously, and how Nasafi argues against the Mu'tazilite claim of precedence.

Core Idea
Created power is simultaneous with the act because it is for acquisition, not creation.

Imam Nasafi addresses a foundational debate in kalam: does the created power (qudra) precede the act, or do they occur together? While the Mu'tazila require precedence because they see power as creative, the Maturidis maintain simultaneity because created power simply makes the act an acquisition (kasb). In this passage, Nasafi presents a careful argument using logical dilemmas and everyday analogies to prove that power and act must coexist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and the English translation side by side. Try to grasp the overall flow before diving into details.
Notice the repeated use of 'maʿan' (together).
2
Identify the central thesis
Locate the statement where Nasafi claims that created power does not precede the act but is simultaneous. Understand the key distinction: power is for acquisition (kasb), not invention (ikhtiraʿ).
This is the core Maturidi position.
3
Follow the dilemma posed to the opponent
Nasafi asks: does power attach to a past act or a future one? Trace how he refutes both options to argue for simultaneity.
The refutation of the past act relies on the non-persistence of accidents.
4
Examine the analogies and the philosophical point
List the examples Nasafi gives: blackness, motion, death, life, etc. Notice how all these pairs exist together. Understand the reference to the philosophers' 'priority in rank' over temporal priority.
These analogies are meant to make the abstract concept intuitive.
5
Understand the refutation of the stalemate
Nasafi rejects the objection that if each requires the other for existence, neither can exist. He explains that in many cases, conditions coexist with the conditioned.
This shows the absurdity of demanding sequentiality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدور، وذلك يوجب سبق القدرة للمقدور ليصبح تأثيرها في العدم، والقدرة المحدثة غير صالحة للاختراع بل هي صالحة لكون المخترع كسبًا للقادر فلم يكن من شرطها التقدم على المقدور، بل من شرطها وجود المخترع ليتعلق بها فيكون كسبًا له، وعن هذا المعنى قيل: إن مسألة الاستطاعة قريبة لمسألة خلق الأفعال، فإن عندهم لما كانت قدرة العبد للاختراع لابد من أن تكون سابقة، وعندنا لما لم تكن للاختراع لم تكن سابقة بل كانت مقارنة لما وجد بالاختراع، ولهذا المعنى جرى العرف من المتكلمين بإيراد هذه المسألة عقيب مسألة خلق أفعال العباد. ثم نقول لهم: إن تعلق القدرة يستحيل بأي موجود؟ بموجود وقع عنه الفراغ؟ أم بموجود لم يقع عنه الفراغ بعد؟ فإن قال بالأول، فهو مسلم غير أن الأعراض ليس لها حالة الفراغ إذ هي الحالة الثانية في حالة الوجود، وهي لا تبقى فتنعدم في تلك الحالة، وإن قال بالثاني فهو غير مسلّم أن القدرة لا تتعلق به ويوجدان معا على ما مر، وهذا هو الجواب عن قولهم: أن القدرة لو كانت توجد مع الفعل لم يكن إضافة الفعل إلى القدرة أولى من إضافة القدرة إلى الفعل فإن السواد باتصاف المحل بكونه أسود، وكذا الحركة مع المتحرك والموت مع الميت والحياة مع الحي العصا اتصافها وخروج من اليد مع الإلقاء، وطلوع الشمس مع وجود النهار كل ذلك يوجدان معاً ولا تخفى العلة والمعلول، ويعرف ببديهة العقل حصول أحدهما بالآخر، واستحالة إضافة العلة إلى الحكم، ولهذا قالت الفلاسفة: العلة متقدمة على المعلول لا تقدماً زمنيًا بل تقدمًا من حيث الرتبة، وحقيقة الكلام ما مر أن حصول العلة في هذه الفصول لو تقدمت لانعدمت وقت حصول المعلول، وحصوله بعلة معدومة غير متصور فلابد من حصولهما معاً، فكذا فيما نحن فيه. وبهذا يبطل ما زعموا أن الفعل لو لم يوجد حتى تحصل القدرة ولن تحصل هي حتى يوجد الفعل لا يتصور وجودهما كما ضرب من المثال، فإن الاتصاف بالسواد مع وجود السواد يوجدان معا ولا يتصور وجود أحدهما بدون ذلك يوجدان، وإنما ذلك فيما يتعلق كل واحد منهما بصاحبه تعلق ومع المشروط بالشرط، فيكون وجود هذا شرطًا لوجود ذلك ووجود ذلك شرطًا لوجود هذا، ووجود المشروط يكون بعد وجود الشرط فيصير شرط وجود كل وحد منهما تقدم صاحبه عليه وهذا محال. فأما فيما يوجدان معا فعليه أكثر الأمور.
The act (al-maqdūr), and that necessitates the precedence of power (al-qudra) over the act so that its effect is in non-existence, but created power (al-qudra al-muḥdatha) is not suitable for invention (al-ikhtirāʿ) rather it is suitable for the invented thing being an acquisition (kasban) for the capable, so it is not required to precede the act, rather it is required that the invented thing exist so that power attaches to it and it becomes an acquisition for him. And from this meaning it was said: The issue of capacity (al-istiṭāʿa) is close to the issue of the creation of actions (khalq al-afʿāl). For according to them, since the servant's power is for invention, it must be prior; according to us, since it is not for invention, it is not prior but is simultaneous (muqārina) with what exists through invention. And for this reason the custom of the mutakallimūn is to bring this issue after the issue of the creation of the actions of servants. Then we say to them: The attachment of power to any existent is impossible? To an existent from which one has become free? Or to an existent from which one has not yet become free? If they say the first, it is granted, but accidents (al-aʿrāḍ) have no state of being free from, for they are the second state in the state of existence, and they do not persist, so they become non-existent in that state. If they say the second, it is not granted that power does not attach to it and they exist together (yūjadān maʿan) as already mentioned. And this is the answer to their saying: If power existed with the act, then the attribution of the act to power would not be more appropriate than the attribution of power to the act. For blackness is with the attribute of the subject being black, and similarly motion with the moving thing, death with the dead, life with the living, the staff with its being in the hand and leaving the hand with throwing, the rising of the sun with the existence of daytime: all of these exist together, and the cause and effect are not hidden, and the occurrence of one by the other is known by the intellect's intuition, and the impossibility of attributing the cause to the judgment. For this reason the philosophers said: the cause precedes the effect not in time but in rank. And the reality of the speech is what has passed: that the occurrence of the cause in these categories, if it preceded, would become non-existent at the time of the occurrence of the effect, and its occurrence by a non-existent cause is inconceivable; so they must exist together. So too in our case. By this is refuted their claim that if the act does not exist until power is acquired and power is not acquired until the act exists, their existence is inconceivable, as they gave an example. For the attribute of blackness with the existence of blackness exists together and it is inconceivable that one exists without that; they exist together. And that is only in what each of them is related to its companion with relation and the conditioned with the condition. So the existence of this is a condition for the existence of that, and the existence of that is a condition for the existence of this. And the existence of the conditioned is after the existence of the condition, so the condition of existence of each one becomes the priority of its companion over it, and this is impossible. As for what exists together, most matters are upon that.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a proof by Imam Nasafi for the simultaneous existence of power (qudra) and act (maqdur), refuting the Mu'tazilite view that power must precede the act. The author begins by stating that if power preceded the act, it would have to affect non-existence, but created power is not creative (ikhtiraʿ); rather it is suitable for the act to become an acquisition (kasb) for the capable agent. Therefore power does not need to precede the act; it only needs the act to exist so it can attach to it. He then links this to the issue of capacity (istitaʿa) and the creation of actions, noting that the Mu'tazila, holding power to be creative, require it to be prior, while the Maturidis hold it simultaneous. Next, Nasafi poses a dilemma for the opponent: does power attach to an act that has already passed or to one that has not yet occurred? If the former, it is impossible because accidents do not persist. If the latter, it is not granted that power cannot attach to it; rather they exist together. He then gives multiple analogies from everyday experience: blackness with the subject being black, motion with the moving thing, death with the dead, etc.—all exist simultaneously, and the causal relationship is known intuitively. He also references the philosophers' distinction between temporal priority and priority in rank. The conclusion is that the cause and effect must coexist; otherwise the cause would be non-existent at the time of the effect. He refutes the hypothetical stalemate where each requires the other to exist first, showing that leads to absurdity. Finally, he asserts that most things in the world exist together (maʿan).

Key Terms
قدرة
مقدور
كسب
استطاعة
اختراع
علة
معلول
شرط
مقارنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power must always precede its object (the act), otherwise causality fails.
Correction: According to Maturidi kalam, created power is not creative but acquisitive, so it does not precede; it coexists with the act. Many causal relationships (e.g., blackness and black object) are simultaneous.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, why does created power (al-qudra al-muḥdatha) not need to precede the act?
A) Because it is creative and thus timeless.
B) Because it is not suitable for invention but for acquisition, so it only needs the act to exist.
C) Because it is eternal and unchanging.
D) Because acts are not real.

Key Takeaway
Created power and its act must coexist because power is for acquisition, not creation, and many causal pairs in nature are simultaneous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an action, do you truly feel that your power to do it is simultaneous with the act itself, or do you sense that your decision comes first? How might this subtle shift in understanding change your reliance on Allah in every moment?
?
The passage teaches that your power is not creative; it merely acquires what Allah creates. Are there areas in your life where you still act as if you are the ultimate creator of your deeds, forgetting that your role is only acquisition? What would change if you internalized that?
?
Nasafi uses everyday examples like blackness and being black to show that cause and effect coexist. Examine one habitual action you performed today—prayer, eating, speaking. Can you see it as simultaneously your act and Allah’s creation? How does that affect your gratitude and humility?

God Describes Himself with Attributes Worthy of Praise
Affirmation that God's attributes are from His own self-description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes are known solely through His own self-description in the Qur'an, and that this is the foundational position of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are as He describes Himself — no more, no less.

This short but foundational passage establishes the bedrock principle of Islamic theology regarding divine attributes. Before we can discuss what Allah is like, we must recognize that only Allah can truly describe Himself. The author anchors this in two Qur'anic verses and then declares it the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice that the author uses two Qur'anic verses to support the point.
The first verse is partially quoted; the second is complete.
2
Identify the two Qur'anic references
The first reference (Surah al-Nur 24:10) speaks of Allah's favor and mercy, and the second (Surah al-Zumar 39:62) describes Allah as Creator and Disposer of all things. Understand how these verses illustrate Allah's self-description.
3
Understand the madhhab statement
The author concludes that this principle (Allah is described as He describes Himself) is the position of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. Reflect on why this is a defining creedal point.
This distinguishes the Sunni approach from those who use human analogy or speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحقيقا لقوله تعالى: وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ . ويستفاد بالثاني معرفة بأن الله تعالى موصوف بما وصف به نفسه محمود به كَمَا قال تعالى: خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَكِيلٌ. هذا هو مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة.
In verification of His saying: "And were it not for the favor of Allah upon you and His mercy..." And by the second [verse] one learns that Allah, exalted, is described with what He described Himself, praised thereby, as He said: "Creator of every thing, and He over every thing is Disposer of affairs." This is the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.

Commentary
This passage affirms that God's attributes are exactly as He has described Himself in the Qur'an. The author quotes two verses: first, a partial quote from Surah al-Nur 24:10 (though the full verse is about Allah's favor and mercy), and second, Surah al-Zumar 39:62 which affirms that Allah is the Creator of all things and the Disposer of all affairs. The point is that Allah is praised specifically with the attributes He uses for Himself, without addition or interpretation. The author concludes that this is the position of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a — i.e., the Maturidi position.

Correction: This passage teaches that Allah is described only as He describes Himself, prohibiting the use of human analogy or speculative reasoning.

Refutation of the Claim that God Creating Insult is Foolish
Imam Nasafi refutes an objection about divine creation of insults.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the objection that God creating insults against Himself would be foolish, by distinguishing between the intrinsic moral quality of an act and the act of creation itself.

Core Idea
God's creation of any act is not judged by the moral quality of that act.

The Mu'tazilites argued that if God were to create insults against Himself, that would be foolish, like a human who slanders himself. Imam Nasafi rejects this analogy, showing that the creation of acts is not subject to the same moral assessment as the acts themselves. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its implications for divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's use of logical connectors like 'فإنه' and 'فحينئذ'.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Find the phrase where the opponent states that creating insult is foolish. Understand the basis of their analogy from the witnessed world.
3
Understand the author's response
The author says the objection is 'corrupt speech' because it presupposes a point of disagreement. Then he gives the alternative interpretation of the verse, showing that it covers all intrinsically good or neutral acts, not immoral ones.
The key is the distinction between the act's own nature and the act of creation.
4
See the conclusion
The author concludes that the verse establishes God's unique praise as the Creator of others' acts, so the objection fails.
This preserves God's transcendence beyond moral categories applied to humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولهم: إن إيجاد شتم نفسه والافتراء عليه سفه استدلالاً بالمتعرض لذلك في الشاهد كلام فاسد، فإنه يتعين بعض فصول ما اختلفنا فيه، وللمتعلق بالآية أن يقول: أنا أستدل بها على كون ما هو مستحسن في نفسه وصواب وحكمة في ذاته من أفعال المكلفين، وكون ما ليس يوصف بالقبح والسفه من أفعالهم وجميع أفعال الحيوانات التي لا تكليف عليها ولا أمر ولا نهي مخلوقا له تعالى بقضية عموم الآية ليثبت التمدح له بما لا يتصور ذلك في غيره، وهو كونه خالقًا لفعل غيره فيحصل ما هو الغرض من الآية، فحينئذ لا يتوجه هذا الاعتراض عليه بوجه من الوجوه.
Their statement: 'Creating insult of Himself and slander against Him is foolishness,' by inferring from one who exposes himself to that in the witnessed world, is corrupt speech. For it determines one of the divisions that we differ on. And the one who adheres to the verse can say: I use it as evidence that what is intrinsically good, correct, and wise among the acts of the morally responsible, and what is not described as ugliness and foolishness among their acts, and all acts of animals that have no obligation nor command nor prohibition, are created by Him, may He be exalted, by virtue of the general meaning of the verse, to establish praise for Him that cannot be conceived for anyone else—namely, His being the Creator of another's act. Thus the purpose of the verse is achieved, and then this objection does not apply to it in any way.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage refutes the objection that if God creates insults against Himself, that would be foolishness (safah). The author first states that the objection is based on an analogy with a human who exposes himself to slander in the witnessed world, which is invalid. The one who holds the verse can argue that the verse's generality shows that all acts that are intrinsically good, correct, wise, or not described as ugly/foolish—including acts of animals without moral responsibility—are created by God. This establishes God's unique praise as the Creator of another's act. Therefore, the objection does not apply.

Key Terms
سفه
شاهد
تمددح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates insults against Himself, then He is foolish, just as a human who does so is foolish.
Correction: God's act of creation is not analogous to a human's act of self-insult because moral categories apply differently to the Creator. The creation of any act is not inherently good or evil; it is the act itself that may be assessed. God's creating an insult does not make Him foolish; rather, it demonstrates His power as Creator.

Checkpoint

B) By distinguishing between intrinsically good and evil acts.
C) By saying the verse only applies to animals.
D) By accepting the claim but justifying it.

Key Takeaway
God's creation of any act does not attribute imperfection to Him because the act of creation is not morally assessed by the nature of the created act.

Refuting the Claim of Specification from the Verse 'Khaliq kulli shay''
The author refutes the claim that the verse is specified to exclude God's essence but not created acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Māturīdī argument that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' does not necessitate excluding created acts, and how the purpose of praise (tamadduḥ) is key.

Core Idea
The same reason that excludes God from the verse demands including created acts.

The verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' (Creator of everything) is often cited by those who deny that humans create their own actions. They claim it is specified to exclude God's essence and attributes, and by analogy to exclude created acts. This passage from Imam al-Nasafī refutes that claim by examining the purpose of the verse: praise (tamadduḥ). By understanding why God's essence is excluded, we see that created acts cannot be excluded without negating the praise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponents' claim
The opponents argue that the verse is specified (makhṣūṣ) to exclude God's essence, and by analogy, created acts are also excluded.
This is a common Ashʿarī argument.
2
Grasp the initial refutation using the analogy of the house
The author gives an example of a person who says he struck everyone in a house but did not strike himself; this does not make the statement specified. Similarly, God's exclusion does not affect generality.
3
Understand the concession and deeper argument
Even if we grant specification, the specification of God does not entail specification of created acts. The core is the purpose of praise.
4
Follow the tamadduḥ argument
Including God under creation would negate praise, so He is excluded. But excluding created acts would also negate praise, so they must be included.
5
Recognize the conclusion and the objection
The author concludes that the opponents are using an evidence that necessitates the opposite. The passage ends with an objection that the inclusion of created acts is also impossible; but the answer is cut off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولذا لم يكن الله تعالى مر بلفظة العلماء والوكلاء ولم يكن خروجه منها سالبًا عموم اللفظ فكذا فيما نحن فيه فدل أن ادعاء الخصوص في هذه الآية صدر عن الجهل بهذه الحقائق على أن الخصوص هو إخراج ما يوجب ظاهر الكلام دخوله فيه وهو لا يوجب دخول المخاطب فيه. ألا ترى أن من قال: دخلت الدار وضربت جميع من فيها وأخرجتهم منها لا يوجب ذلك دخوله فيه وخروجه منه لا يعد خصوصا فكذا هذا، على أنا وإن يوجب ساعدناهم في كون الآية مخصوصة، ولكن خصوص الباري سبحانه وتعالى لا يوجب خصوص أفعال الخلق بل يوجب امتناع خروجه، ومن ظن وجوب حصول شيء بالدليل الموجب امتناع حصوله فهو مغفل جاهل بالوجوب والامتناع، وإنما قلنا: إن خروج ذات الباري جلا وعلا عن قضية الآية لا يوجب خروج المتنازع فيه لأن دخول ذات الباري تحت قضية الآية لا يوجب زوال ما هو الغرض بالآية، وهو التمدح إذ لا تمدح يحصل بدخول ذاته تحت قدرة التخليق بل يزول به التمدح فخرج عن الآية لئلا يزول ما هو الغرض من الآية، وليس في دخول المتنازع فيه تحت الآية ما يوجب زوال ما الغرض على ما قررنا، فالقول بوجوب الخروج عن الآية لما لم يقم دليل خروجه عنها استدلالاً بخروج ما قام دليل خروجه عنها تحكم ظاهر، وأما دعوانا قيام دليل امتناع خروج المتنازع فيه عن الآية فلما سبق من القول أن الآية وردت على طريق التمدح وخروج المتنازع فيه عنها يوجب زوال معنى التمدح لما أنه يصير كأنه قال خالق كل شيء ليس يفعل غيره ويساويه في هذه الرتبة كل ما دب ودرج وذا فاسد، فإذا تبين أن عين المعنى الذي يوجب خروج ذات الباري وصفاته عن الآية وهو خروج الآية مخرج التمدح يوجب استحالة خروج المتنازع فيه عنها، فمن أوجب خروج المتنازع فهي عن الآية بخروج ذات الباري وصفاته عنها فهو موجب حصول الشيء بالدليل الموجب امتناع حصوله وهو جهل مفرط. وبهذا يجاب من زعم منهم أن خروج ذات الباري تعالى عن مقتضى الآية كان لما في دخوله تحتها من الاستحالة ودخول أفعال العباد مستحيل، فيقال:
For this reason, Allah Most High was not intended by the word 'scholars' and 'agents' and His exclusion from it does not negate the generality of the word; likewise in our case. So it indicates that claiming specification (takhṣīṣ) in this verse originated from ignorance of these realities. Indeed, specification is the exclusion of what the apparent meaning of the statement necessitates its inclusion, and it does not necessitate the inclusion of the addressee in it. Do you not see that whoever says: 'I entered the house and struck all who were in it and expelled them from it' does not necessitate that he himself entered it, and his exit from it is not considered specification? So too this. Even if we grant that the verse is specified, but the specification of the Exalted Lord does not necessitate the specification of the acts of creatures; rather it necessitates the impossibility of His exclusion. And whoever thinks that something is necessitated by an evidence that necessarily necessitates its impossibility is a confused ignorant of necessity and impossibility. And we only say: Indeed, the exclusion of the essence of the Lord, exalted, from the purport of the verse does not necessitate the exclusion of the disputed matter (al-mutanāzaʿ fīhi) because the inclusion of His essence under the purport of the verse does not necessitate the removal of what is the purpose of the verse, which is praise (tamadduḥ). For no praise is obtained by the inclusion of His essence under the power of creation; rather praise is removed by it. So He was excluded from the verse so that the purpose of the verse is not removed. And there is nothing in the inclusion of the disputed matter under the verse that necessitates the removal of the purpose, as we established. So the claim that it is necessary to exclude from the verse what has no evidence for its exclusion, by analogy to the exclusion of what has evidence for its exclusion, is manifest arbitrariness. As for our claim that there is evidence for the impossibility of the exclusion of the disputed matter from the verse, it is because of what preceded from our statement that the verse came in the mode of praise, and the exclusion of the disputed matter from it would necessitate the removal of the meaning of praise, because it would become as if He said: 'Creator of everything, He does nothing other than it, and everything that creeps and crawls equals Him in this rank' — and that is corrupt. So when it is clear that the very meaning that necessitates the exclusion of the essence of the Lord and His attributes from the verse — which is that the verse came in the mode of praise — necessitates the impossibility of the exclusion of the disputed matter from it, then whoever necessitates the exclusion of the disputed matter from the verse by analogy to the exclusion of the essence of the Lord and His attributes from it, he is one who necessitates the occurrence of a thing by an evidence that necessarily necessitates its impossibility, and that is extreme ignorance. And by this, it is answered to those who claim from them that the exclusion of the essence of the Lord Most High from the purport of the verse was due to the impossibility in His inclusion under it, and the inclusion of the acts of servants is impossible, so it is said:
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' is specified (makhṣūṣ) to exclude God's essence and attributes, and that by analogy created acts are also excluded. The author first argues that the exclusion of God from the verse does not affect its generality, using the analogy of a person who says he struck everyone in a house but did not strike himself. He then concedes that if the verse is specified, the specification of God does not necessitate specification of created acts; rather it necessitates the impossibility of His exclusion. The core of the argument is the purpose of the verse: praise (tamadduḥ). Including God's essence under 'power of creation' would negate praise, so He is excluded. But excluding created acts would also negate praise, as it would imply that God does not create everything. Thus, the same reason that excludes God necessitates the inclusion of created acts. The author concludes that whoever excludes created acts by analogy is ignorantly using an evidence that necessitates the opposite. The passage ends with an objection that the exclusion of God is due to impossibility, and that including created acts is also impossible; the author begins his answer with 'fa-yuqālu:' but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
خصوص
التمدح
خالق كل شيء
المتنازع فيه
ذات الباري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since God's essence cannot be included in the verse due to impossibility, created acts should also be excluded as impossible.
Correction: The exclusion of God's essence is due to the purpose of praise, not impossibility per se. Including created acts does not negate praise; rather, excluding them would. So the same reasoning leads to inclusion, not exclusion.

Checkpoint
What is the core reason the author gives for excluding God's essence from the verse?
A) Impossibility of God being a creator
B) To preserve the purpose of praise (tamadduḥ)
C) Because the verse is abrogated
D) Because God is not a thing

Key Takeaway
The same purpose of praise that excludes God from the verse demands the inclusion of created acts; otherwise, the praise would be negated.

God's Exclusion Includes Human Acts
Imam al-Nasafi argues that God's unique status does not exclude human actions from the verse's scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that the very reason for God's exclusion from the verse 'Creator of everything' (preserving praise) necessitates the inclusion of human acts under the same verse.

Core Idea
The same proof that excludes God includes human acts.

Imam al-Nasafi tackles a key objection: if the verse 'Creator of everything' is specifically about God, doesn't that mean human actions are not created by God? He shows that the verse's purpose—praise—drives a precise logic: God's essence is excluded to preserve praise, but human acts must be included for the same reason. This lesson unpacks that subtle argument, revealing a powerful kalam method of interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Imam al-Nasafi first concedes a point to the opponents (the verse is specific to God) but then redefines what that specificity means.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two main claims: (1) God's uniqueness does not necessitate excluding human acts; (2) The same reason that excludes God actually proves human acts must be included. Find where each claim is stated.
3
Understand the logic of praise
The author argues that the verse is in the mode of praise (tamaddḥ). Ask yourself: Why would including God under the verse remove praise? And why would excluding human acts also remove praise? Trace his reasoning.
This is the heart of the argument.
4
See the refutation of the opponent
The author concludes by calling the opponent's position 'extreme ignorance.' How does he show that arguing by analogy from God's exclusion fails?
He shows that the same proof that excludes God makes the opponent's analogy self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساعدناهم في كون الآية مخصوصة، ولكن خصوص الباري سبحانه وتعالى لا يوجب خصوص أفعال الخلق بل يوجب امتناع خروجه، ومن ظن وجوب حصول شيء بالدليل الموجب امتناع حصوله فهو مغفل جاهل بالوجوب والامتناع، وإنما قلنا: إن خروج ذات الباري جلا وعلا عن قضية الآية لا يوجب خروج المتنازع فيه لأن دخول ذات الباري تحت قضية الآية لا يوجب زوال ما هو الغرض بالآية، وهو التمدح إذ لا تمدح يحصل بدخول ذاته تحت قدرة التخليق بل يزول به التمدح فخرج عن الآية لئلا يزول ما هو الغرض من الآية، وليس في دخول المتنازع فيه تحت الآية ما يوجب زوال ما الغرض على ما قررنا، فالقول بوجوب الخروج عن الآية لما لم يقم دليل خروجه عنها استدلالاً بخروج ما قام دليل خروجه عنها تحكم ظاهر، وأما دعوانا قيام دليل امتناع خروج المتنازع فيه عن الآية فلما سبق من القول أن الآية وردت على طريق التمدح وخروج المتنازع فيه عنها يوجب زوال معنى التمدح لما أنه يصير كأنه قال خالق كل شيء ليس يفعل غيره ويساويه في هذه الرتبة كل ما دب ودرج وذا فاسد، فإذا تبين أن عين المعنى الذي يوجب خروج ذات الباري وصفاته عن الآية وهو خروج الآية مخرج التمدح يوجب استحالة خروج المتنازع فيه عنها، فمن أوجب خروج المتنازع فهي عن الآية بخروج ذات الباري وصفاته عنها فهو موجب حصول الشيء بالدليل الموجب امتناع حصوله وهو جهل مفرط.
We helped them [the opponents] in that the verse is specific (makhṣūṣah), but the specificity (khuṣūṣ) of God—glorified and exalted—does not necessitate the specificity of the acts of creatures, rather it necessitates the impossibility of His exclusion. Whoever thinks that something is necessary by a proof that necessitates its impossibility is a heedless ignoramus concerning necessity and impossibility. We only said: the exclusion of God’s essence—majestic and exalted—from the scope of the verse does not necessitate the exclusion of the disputed [human acts], because the inclusion of God’s essence under the scope of the verse does not necessitate the removal of what is the purpose of the verse, which is praise (tamaddḥ). For no praise occurs by the inclusion of His essence under the power of creation (takhliq), rather praise would be removed by it. So He was excluded from the verse lest the purpose of the verse be removed. And in the inclusion of the disputed [human acts] under the verse there is nothing that necessitates the removal of the purpose, as we have established. Thus the claim that the disputed must be excluded from the verse because no proof of its exclusion has been established, by analogy with the exclusion of what a proof of its exclusion has been established, is pure arbitrariness. As for our claim that a proof exists for the impossibility of excluding the disputed from the verse, it is due to what preceded: that the verse was revealed in the mode of praise, and excluding the disputed from it would necessitate the removal of the meaning of praise, because it would become as if He said: 'Creator of everything' but He does not do [created acts other than His?] and everything that creeps and crawls would equal Him in this rank—and that is corrupt. So when it is clear that the very meaning that necessitates the exclusion of God’s essence and attributes from the verse—namely that the verse is in the mode of praise—necessitates the impossibility of excluding the disputed from it, then whoever necessitates the exclusion of the disputed from the verse by virtue of the exclusion of God’s essence and attributes from it is one who necessitates the occurrence of a thing by a proof that necessitates its impossibility, and that is extreme ignorance.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument (proof) regarding the interpretation of the verse "Creator of everything" (Qur'an 39:62). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, first concedes that the verse is specific to God (makhṣūṣah) in a certain sense, but he immediately distinguishes: God's specific uniqueness (khuṣūṣ) does not imply that the acts of creatures are excluded from the verse's scope. Rather, it necessitates the impossibility of excluding God. He then rebukes anyone who thinks that a proof requiring something's impossibility could make it necessary—such a person is confused. He explains that God's essence was excluded from the verse (i.e., the verse does not mean that God is under any power of creation) because including Him would remove the purpose of the verse, which is praise (tamaddḥ). If God were described as being under a power of creation, that would not be praise. Therefore, God was excluded. However, including human acts under the verse does not remove the purpose; rather, excluding them would destroy the praise, because it would imply that other beings are like God in creating. Thus, the same reason that excludes God (the mode of praise) actually necessitates including human acts. Anyone who argues that human acts are excluded by analogy with God's exclusion fails to see that the proof for excluding God is the same proof that makes exclusion of human acts impossible.

Key Terms
خصوص (specialization)
تمدد (praise)
خروج (exclusion)
استحالة (impossibility)
تمنع (prevention)
مغفل (heedless)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because God is unique and excluded from the verse's scope, human acts are also excluded.
Correction: God's exclusion is due to preserving praise; the same reason requires including human acts, as excluding them would destroy the praise.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that God's essence is excluded from the verse (i.e., the verse does not imply God is under a power of creation)?
A) Because God is not a creator.
B) Because including God would remove the purpose of praise.
C) Because God cannot be described.
D) Because the verse only applies to bodies.

Key Takeaway
The very purpose of praise that excludes God from the verse requires the inclusion of human acts under it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Creator of everything,' do you truly believe that your own actions—every word, every step—are included under His creation? Or do you live as if some of your deeds originate from you alone? What would change in your daily life if you fully internalized that lesson?
?
Imam al-Nasafi argues that excluding human acts from the verse would destroy God's praise by making others equal to Him. Honestly, when you succeed or do good, do you subtly attribute it to your own ability, thereby robbing God of His exclusive praise? Will you now consciously redirect every success back to Him?
?
The proof hinges on preserving the purpose of praise. Examine your worship: is your prayer, your charity, your patience aimed at praising God alone, or do you seek the praise of people? How does this lesson expose the idolatry of seeking human approval, and what concrete step will you take today to purify your intention?

Refuting the Impossibility of Including Human Acts
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the claim of impossibility and examines three proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi refutes the claim that including human acts in the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' is impossible, by examining three proposed proofs.

Core Idea
Including human acts in God's creation is not impossible; it would destroy the praise in the verse.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi addresses the objection that God's essence is excluded from the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' because including it would be impossible, and that including human acts is similarly impossible. He responds by showing that the verse itself disproves this claim, and then systematically challenges three possible proofs for impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
First, read the objection as presented by the opponents: that including God and human acts in the verse is impossible. Grasp the initial answer: the verse itself shows this is not impossible because it would negate praise.
2
Examine the three proofs
The author asks for evidence of impossibility. Three proofs are considered: (1) God's wisdom preventing creation of evil, (2) two agents on one act, (3) ugliness of acts. Notice the author's response to each.
The first proof is already answered; the second is refuted by the verse's scope; the third is addressed by distinguishing between the act's ugliness and the creation of it.
3
Understand the deferment
The author defers a fuller rational explanation to later discussion. This shows the methodology of kalam: some points require deeper metaphysical argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يجاب من زعم منهم أن خروج ذات الباري تعالى عن مقتضى الآية كان لما في دخوله تحتها من الاستحالة ودخول أفعال العباد مستحيل، فيقال: ورود الآية يدل أن دخول أفعال الخلق ليس بمستحيل لأن جعل ذلك مستحيلاً يوجب التسوية بينه وبين ما دب ودرج وذا يزيل معنى التمدح الذي سيقت له الآية، على أنا نسألهم عن دليل الاستحالة فإن قالوا: دليل استحالة ذلك [؟] كون الباري حكيمًا فلا يليق به تخلیق شتم نفسه، فقد أجبنا عنه، وإن جعلوا دليل الاستحالة دخول مقدور تحت قدرة قادرين فنقول: مورد الآية يقتضي نفي الاستحالة لما في ثبوت استحالة زوال معنى التمدح على أنا نبين أن ذلك ليس بمستحيل إذا شرعنا في المعقول إن شاء الله تعالى - على أن إقامة دليل الاستحالة عليهم لا علينا، وإن جعلوا دليل الاستحالة قبح هذه الأفعال بقيت الآية حجة في ما ليس بقبيح من أفعال الخلق على أن إيجاد القبيح ليس بقبيح في المعقول، إذ تحصيل الشيء على ما ينبغي أن يكون عليه من حسن وقبح حكمة، كما أن العلم به على ما هو عليه علم وليس بجهل، ونبين حقيقة هذا الكلام إذا انتهينا إلى المعقول في المسألة - إن شاء الله. وليس يستقيم قولهم إن قوله تعالى: خلق كل شيء ورد في الأجسام دون الأعراض، لأن المنازعة في تخليق الأفعال ما كانت ثابتة في زمن النبي عليه السلام بل حدثت بعد ذلك، وإنما الخلاف في ذلك الزمان كان بين الموحدين وبين الثنوية والمجوس والزنادقة في تخليق الأجسام الضارة، فوردت الآية لبيان ذلك لأنا نقول: الخلاف في خلق الأفعال كان [؟] في ذلك الزمان وقبل ذلك الزمان، فإن طائفة من اليهود يقال لهم: العنانية كانوا على ما ذهبت إليه المعتزلة، وأكثر النصارى كانت تقول بالجبر، فإذا هذه دعوة كاذبة، على أنا نقول: هب أن الخلاف في هذه
And by this is answered the one among them who claims that the exclusion of God’s essence—exalted—from the implication of the verse was due to the impossibility of including Him under it, and that including the acts of servants is impossible. So it is said: The revelation of the verse indicates that the inclusion of the acts of creatures is not impossible, because making that impossible would necessitate equating Him with everything that creeps and crawls, and that would remove the meaning of praise for which the verse was brought. Moreover, we ask them for the proof of impossibility: if they say, 'The proof of the impossibility of that [is] that God is wise (ḥakīm), so it is not befitting for Him to create insults against Himself,' we have already answered that. And if they make the proof of impossibility the inclusion of an object of power under the power of two agents, we say: The scope of the verse necessitates denying impossibility, because [otherwise] there would be the establishment of the impossibility of the removal of the meaning of praise. And we will show that this is not impossible when we come to the rational discussion (al-ma‘qūl), God willing. Moreover, establishing the proof of impossibility is incumbent on them, not on us. And if they make the proof of impossibility the ugliness (qubḥ) of these acts, the verse remains a proof concerning what is not ugly among the acts of creatures—since the creation of the ugly is not ugly in reason, because bringing about a thing as it should be—whether good or ugly—is wisdom, just as knowledge of it as it is is knowledge and not ignorance. And we will explain the reality of this statement when we reach the rational discussion on the issue, God willing. And their statement that the verse 'Creator of everything' was revealed concerning bodies and not accidents is not sound, because the dispute about the creation of acts was not established in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, but occurred after that. Rather, the disagreement at that time was between the monotheists and the dualists, Magians, and heretics (zanādiqah) concerning the creation of harmful bodies, so the verse was revealed to clarify that. But we say: The disagreement about the creation of acts existed in that time and before that time. Indeed, a sect of the Jews called al-‘Anāniyyah held the position of the Mu‘tazila, and most Christians held to determinism (jabr). So this claim is false. Moreover, we say: Grant that the disagreement [is about this...]
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a historical argument. First, the author (Imam al-Nasafi) addresses an opponent's claim: that God was excluded from the verse because including Him was impossible, and similarly including human acts is impossible. The answer is that the verse itself shows that including human acts is not impossible, because deeming it impossible would equate creatures with God in a way that destroys the praise (tamaddḥ). Then the author asks for the proof of impossibility. Three possible proofs are considered: (1) God's wisdom preventing Him from creating evil (like insults against Himself)—already answered; (2) two agents on one act—the verse's scope denies impossibility because otherwise praise would be removed; (3) the ugliness of acts—the verse still applies to non-ugly acts, and creating the ugly is not itself ugly in reason, because wisdom consists in making things as they should be. The author defers fuller rational discussion. Second, the author refutes the claim that the verse only refers to bodies, not accidents (like actions). He argues historically: the early dispute (at the time of the Prophet) was between monotheists and dualists/Magians about the creation of harmful bodies; later disputes about actions arose later. However, he counters that the dispute about actions existed even earlier: a Jewish sect (al-‘Anāniyyah) held Mu‘tazilite views, and most Christians held determinism. Thus the opponents' claim is false. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main points are clear.

Key Terms
استحالة
تمدد
حكيم
قبيح
مقدور
قادرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Including human acts in God's creation is impossible because those acts are evil or because it would require two agents.
Correction: The author shows that the verse's praise of God as Creator of all things would be negated if human acts were excluded, and each proof of impossibility is refuted.

Checkpoint
What is the author's response to the third proof of impossibility (ugliness of acts)?
A) He agrees that God cannot create ugly acts.
B) He says the verse only applies to good acts.
C) He argues that creating the ugly is not ugly in reason, and the verse remains a proof for non-ugly acts.
D) He defers the answer to rational discussion.

Key Takeaway
The verse's inclusive scope refutes the claim of impossibility; the creation of all acts is not impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the idea that God creates even your worst actions make you feel about your responsibility for them? Do you tend to blame God for your sins, or do you accept full accountability?
?
If creating evil is not itself evil for God, how does that affect the way you view the presence of evil in the world? Can you still trust God's wisdom when you see injustice?
?
The author argues that wisdom is bringing about things as they should be. Can you point to a specific event in your life that seemed ugly but you now believe was placed exactly as it should be by God? What would it take for you to reach that conviction?

Historical Context of the Verse 'Khaliq Kulli Shay'
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the limitation of the verse to bodies using historical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical debate about the verse's scope and how Imam al-Nasafi argues that it includes human actions, based on early disputes.

Core Idea
The verse was revealed for bodies, but earlier disputes about actions prove its wider scope.

Imam al-Nasafi now addresses the claim that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' was revealed only for bodies, not for human actions. He argues that the dispute about the creation of actions existed even before the Prophet's time among Jews and Christians, so the verse's scope is not limited.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's claim
The opponents say the verse was revealed specifically about bodies, not accidents like human actions. Read this claim carefully.
2
Identify the author's initial refutation
The author first notes that the dispute about actions arose after the Prophet, and the early dispute was about bodies. But then he counters that the dispute about actions actually existed earlier.
This is a nuanced argument: the author seems to first concede, then rebut.
3
Examine the historical evidence
The author cites a Jewish sect (al-‘Anāniyyah) that held Mu'tazilite views on human acts, and most Christians held to determinism. This shows that the issue was not new, so the verse can include actions.
The passage ends mid-conclusion, but the main point is clear.

The Proof Holds Even for the Acted Upon
Nasafi shows the argument for created actions holds even on Mu'tazila interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi's argument for the createdness of human actions remains valid even if the Quranic phrase 'ma ta'malun' is interpreted as referring to the thing acted upon rather than the action itself.

Core Idea
The object's creation necessitates the action's creation.

The Mu'tazila might object that the verse 'wa-llahu khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun' refers to the objects you make, not your actions. Nasafi grants this interpretation for argument's sake but shows the proof still holds. If God creates the thing acted upon, He must also create the action that produces it, because the object cannot exist without the action. This lesson unpacks that logical move.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concession
Nasafi begins by conceding the Mu'tazila interpretation: the verse could mean 'God created you and your thing acted upon.' This is a hypothetical concession to test their logic.
The concession is strategic—it does not mean Nasafi agrees.
2
Identify the dependency
He then argues that the thing acted upon depends on the action of the servants. Without the action, the body would not become a 'thing acted upon' (e.g., an idol carved by human effort).
Focus on the relationship between the object and the action.
3
Trace the logical inference
Since God affirms that He creates the thing acted upon, and the thing acted upon is only a thing acted upon through the action, it follows that the action itself must also be created by God.
This is a necessary entailment, not a mere possibility.
4
Apply the conclusion
The proof that human actions are created by God remains intact, regardless of how 'ma ta'malun' is interpreted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنا وإن صرفنا الآية إلى المعمول، وجعلنا كأنه قال: والله خلقكم ومعمولكم فالاستدلال بالآية باق لأن الله تعالى لم يكن خالقا للمعمول لو لم يكن عملهم مخلوقا له لأن ذلك الجسم بدون عمل العباد لا وهو تعالى أثبت الخلق للمعمول فدل أن العمل الذي صار به الجسم المخلوق معمولاً كان مخلوقاً له، حتى جعل المعمول مخلوقا له والله الموفق.
Even if we turn the verse to the thing acted upon (al-ma'mul), and make it as if He said: 'And God created you and your thing acted upon,' then the inference by the verse remains, because God exalted would not have been Creator of the thing acted upon if their action (amaluhum) was not created by Him, because that body without the action of the servants does not [become a thing acted upon], and He exalted affirmed creation for the thing acted upon, so it indicates that the action by which the created body became a thing acted upon was created by Him, so that He made the thing acted upon created by Him, and God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal to the Mu'tazila's possible objection. The author concedes, for argument's sake, that the phrase 'ما تعملون' in the verse might refer to the thing acted upon (المعمول) rather than the action. Even then, the inference that actions are created by God remains valid. If God is the Creator of the thing acted upon (e.g., the carved idol), then He must also be the Creator of the action that makes it a thing acted upon. The body without the action of the servants would not become a thing acted upon. Since God affirms creating the thing acted upon, it necessarily follows that the action (العمل) by which the body becomes a thing acted upon is also created by God. Thus, the argument is preserved.

Key Terms
المعمول
العمل
خلق
الاستدلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the verse 'wa ma ta'malun' refers to the thing acted upon, then the proof that actions are created by God fails.
Correction: Even if the verse refers to the thing acted upon, the proof still holds because the object's creation depends on the action; if God creates the object, He must create the action that produces it.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi say the proof remains even if 'ما تعملون' means the thing acted upon?
A) Because the thing acted upon cannot exist without the action, and God creates both.
B) Because the verse only mentions objects, not actions.
C) Because the Mu'tazila agree that actions are not created.
D) Because the thing acted upon is not created by God.

Key Takeaway
The creation of the thing acted upon logically entails the creation of the action that produces it, so the proof for created actions remains valid even under the Mu'tazila interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you truly believe that even that action is created by Allah, or do you subtly attribute it to your own ability? How can you train your heart to see every good action as a gift from Him?
?
Reflect on a sin you have committed. If your very action in that moment was created by Allah, how does that reshape your understanding of repentance? Does it make you more humble, knowing that even your rebellion is within His dominion?
?
This passage shows that even the interpretation of the verse that seems to avoid the conclusion still leads to it. Are there areas in your life where you twist meanings to avoid acknowledging Allah's complete control? What would it cost you to surrender that last area?

The Metaphorical Use of 'خالق' for Humans
Explains that 'خلق' can mean 'تقدير', allowing metaphorical attribution of 'خالق' to humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ' is interpreted to allow a metaphorical attribution of 'خالق' to humans, without compromising the exclusive creative power of Allah.

Core Idea
'خلق' can mean estimation, not just creation, so calling humans 'خالق' is metaphorical.

This passage tackles a potential proof used by some Mu'tazilites who claimed that the Qur'anic phrase 'the best of creators' implies that humans can be creators in a real sense. The author refutes this by showing that the word 'خلق' has a broader meaning that includes estimation and forming, not just bringing into existence. Through linguistic analysis and poetic examples, he demonstrates that the verse does not grant humans independent creative power.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the Mu'tazilite claim
Begin by reading the verse 'أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ' and understand how some Mu'tazilites used it to argue that humans can be creators.
This sets up the problem the author is addressing.
2
Understand the refutation
The author explains that 'خلق' can mean 'تقدير' (estimation) and 'تصوير' (forming), not just 'اختراع' (invention) or 'إيجاد' (bringing into existence). This allows a metaphorical sense.
This is the core linguistic argument.
3
Examine the linguistic evidence
Look at the poet's line and the analogies of 'the two Umars' and 'two moons'. These show that a term can apply in a restricted sense when linked to another.
The analogies clarify the metaphorical nature.
4
Apply the principle
Reflect on how this principle protects tawhid: only Allah is the true creator; any attribution to humans is metaphorical and dependent on the divine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناقشة في آية (فَتَبَارَكَ اللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ): ثم المتعلق من أوائل البصرية وجميع البغدادية منهم بقوله تعالى: أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ ليس بصحيح لمساعدتهم إيانا على أن من سوى الله تعالى ليس بخالق ويستحيل وصف من سواه به ولو تعلق بذلك متأخرو أهل البصرة المجوزون ذلك يقال لهم: الخلق يذكر ويراد به التقدير والتصوير دون الاختراع والإيجاد، وعلى هذا التقدير يجوز أن يسمى العبد خالقا قال قائلهم: ولأنت تفري ما خلقت وبعض القوم يخلق ثم لا يفري فكانت الآية محمولة عليه دفعًا للتناقض عن الآيات والدلائل، على أن العبد يكون فاعلاً ولا يكون خالقًا، والله تعالى هو الخالق، ويجوز إطلاق اسم الخالق على العبد وإن لم يكن خالقا إذا ضم إلى الخالق كما يقال: سنة العمرين في أبي بكر رضي الله عنهما – وإن كان أبو بكر لا يسمى عند الانفراد عمر، وكذا يقال للشمس والقمر قمران قال القائل: أخذنا بآفاق السماء عليكم لنا قمراها والنجوم الطوالع وإن كان اسم القمر لا يطلق على الشمس عند الانفراد فكذا هذا، والله الموفق.
Discussion on the verse 'So blessed be Allah, the best of creators.' Then the attachment of the early Basrans and all the Baghdadis among them to His statement, the Exalted, 'the best of creators' is not correct because they agree with us that other than Allah is not a creator and it is impossible to describe other than Him with it. Even if later Basrans who allow that were to cling to it, it is said to them: 'خلق' is used and meant by it 'تقدير' (estimation) and 'تصوير' (forming) without invention and bringing into existence. On this estimation, it is permissible to call the servant a 'خالق'. Their poet said: 'And you cut what you created, while some people create but do not cut.' So the verse is carried upon that to prevent contradiction between verses and proofs. The servant is an agent but not a creator, and Allah is the Creator. It is permissible to apply the name 'خالق' to the servant even though he is not a creator when linked to the Creator, just as it is said 'the sunna of the two 'Umars' regarding Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with them, even though Abu Bakr is not called 'Umar when alone; and likewise the sun and moon are called 'two moons' as the poet said: 'We took from the horizons of the sky upon you, we have its two moons and the rising stars' even though the name 'moon' is not applied to the sun when alone. So is this. And Allah grants success.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a claim based on the verse 'أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ'. The author argues that the Mu'tazilites cannot use this verse to prove humans are creators in the absolute sense because they themselves agree that only Allah is creator. He explains that 'خلق' can mean estimation (تقدير) and forming (تصوير), not just invention. Thus a human can be called 'خالق' metaphorically, as in the poetry example. He illustrates with analogies: calling Abu Bakr and 'Umar together 'the two 'Umars', and calling the sun and moon 'two moons' in poetry. This shows that a term can apply in a restricted sense when linked to another, without implying independent status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ' proves that humans are creators in the absolute sense, independent of Allah.
Correction: The word 'خلق' in the verse means estimation and forming, not creation ex nihilo, and the attribution to humans is metaphorical, as demonstrated by linguistic usage and analogies like 'the two Umars'.

Checkpoint
According to the author, in what sense can a human be called 'خالق'?
A) In the sense of independent creation ex nihilo.
B) In the sense of estimation and forming (تقدير وتصوير) without invention.
C) In the sense of being a partner to God in creation.
D) In the sense of having power over one's own actions.

Key Takeaway
Calling a human 'خالق' is permissible only in a metaphorical sense of estimation and forming, not as an independent creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you create or produce something in your daily life—whether a project at work, a meal, or a relationship—do you ever catch yourself feeling a sense of absolute ownership or power over that outcome, forgetting that your ability is merely borrowed and limited? In what specific moments this week can you remind yourself that you are only an agent (فاعل), not a creator in the true sense?
?
This lesson teaches that the word 'خلق' can be used for humans only in a metaphorical sense of estimation and forming. Think of a situation where you used the word 'create' about yourself or heard others use it. How does this linguistic precision change the way you view your own accomplishments? Are there any areas of your life where you have subtly attributed to yourself a power that belongs only to Allah?
?
The analogy of the two 'Umars' shows that a human can be called 'خالق' only when linked to the Creator. Are there any names or descriptions you accept about yourself that, without being connected to Allah, would be false or even transgressing His exclusive attributes? How can you more consciously anchor your identity and achievements to Allah rather than to yourself alone?
